Current Commentary

The Resumption of U.S.-Soviet Relations and the Obscurity of Japanese-Soviet Relations

(I) The Abnormal Relationship Between the United States and the Soviet Union

The United States' recognition of the Soviet Union and the resumption of normal diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union have recently become one of the world's focuses. Most people in the United States tend to pay more attention to domestic issues, especially the so-called prosperity of the market, and are not very concerned about general world issues. Furthermore, the Monroe Doctrine is its traditional foreign policy. The countries of the European continent owe the United States more than 10 billion in war debts, and there is a lack of full understanding and experience of them. Let alone the Soviet Union, which is a unique new country in this era, it is normal that it is not easily understood. However, the discord between the United States and the Soviet Union, the fact that the United States has not yet recognized the Soviet Union, and the absence of diplomatic relations, while there are personal exchanges, besides the emotional clash, the Baku oil field stock issue is the real focus.

However, factual needs and the force of the general trend make it impossible for individuals or a small number of people to forcibly prevent it. Therefore, even if there are no diplomatic relations between the United States and the Soviet Union to guarantee, and the Soviet Union is clearly governed by communists, the trade between the United States and the Soviet Union has the greatest risk on the surface, and the safety of capital will hardly be guaranteed. However, since the consolidation of the Soviet Union's national foundation and the implementation of the Five-Year Plan, its trade with the United States has improved daily. The reason why American goods exported to the Soviet Union fell to 24 million rubles last year was probably due to market competition from Britain and Germany, and economic panic was also a factor in the decline of trade. However, the United States' desire to open up markets to reduce the tide of its economic panic, restore past prosperity, and seek a new balance of capitalism has not been forgotten for a moment. Moreover, the main industries of the American industrial sector are mostly heavy industries such as steel and machinery, and what the Soviet Union urgently needs is also machinery, steel, and the technology of advanced capitalist countries. This is precisely what the United States has in abundance and is eager to export. However, the situation on the European continent is most noteworthy. First, Hitler is in power, acting arbitrarily, and strongly denouncing the Treaty of Versailles. He also demands equality in the matter of armaments. In international relations, he is mainly allied with Italy, which will develop into a fascist international organization. However, he is still secretly working with financial capitalists to form the highest stage of financial capital dictatorship. In domestic construction, he still cannot avoid following in the footsteps of Papen's economic policy. The Weimar Constitution (democracy) will retire, and harsh and ruthless blows and suppression will be imposed on the Social Democratic Party and the Communist Party. Its main purpose is to stabilize Hitler's regime. Although the Soviet Union is not as deeply resentful as the Treaty of Versailles, the Soviet-German relations will not proceed as smoothly as in the past. The fact is very obvious that the future Soviet-German economic relations may be affected by political and diplomatic unrest and fall into stagnation. At a time when the United States is encountering

obstacles everywhere, war debts are difficult to recover, foreign investments are frozen, and the financial panic has not ended, can it not seriously consider the resumption of U.S.-Soviet diplomatic relations? There are still more serious problems than those with Western Europe, namely, the Far East problem. The fact that Japan and the Soviet Union already have diplomatic relations and that China's invasion indirectly gives the United States a great blow to opening up the market in China means that the United States should carefully consider its way out.

Japan and the Soviet Union in a Three-Legged Stool 17

It is well known to the world that the relations between Japan and the United States are gradually deteriorating, and there is no need for you to describe it. It is especially clear that exclusive occupation and annexation and equal sharing of interests cannot coexist. If the current system exists in the next few years, this kind of conflict will inevitably not be resolved. At the same time, if China cannot stop this kind of hegemonic military action of the Japanese imperialists with an iron fist, then Britain, the United States, and France will have to temporarily stand by and watch. Even if the United States is extremely angry and extremely disgusted, it will only be angry and disgusted. In addition, it cannot take any further effective action, fearing that this will cause serious consequences and bring unexpected disasters. Therefore, Japan was able to expand the September 18th Incident to North Manchuria, with the intention of seizing the Chinese Eastern Railway as its own. In the past year, although the Soviet Union has repeatedly suggested the signing of a Japanese-Soviet non-aggression treaty, Japan has insisted that there must be exchange conditions, and the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway is one of its important terms. How can the Soviet Union recognize this? However, Japan also has a reason for holding this position. First, its invasion of the Northeast is also appealing to the capitalist countries of the world, saying that it is to prevent the southward invasion of communism and maintain peace in the Orient. Second, it is said to suppress the redification of China, protect the safety of the Far East market, and establish Japan's so-called lifeline. At the same time, when Yosuke Matsuoka passed through the Soviet border, he stayed in the Red Capital, Moscow, for a week to exchange views with Soviet Union's top leaders, seeking understanding between Japan and the Soviet Union. Kojiro Matsukata also bought a lot of red oil, further promoting Japanese-Soviet friendship in fact. From this, it can be seen that Japan is trying to use the close relationship with the Soviet Union to maneuver among the nations, seeking to seize the northern territory of China. However, the Soviet Union has not yet made a definite statement. Judging from past events, it will continue to be cautious and will not act rashly. Its quiet observation is still continuing.

The United States' resumption of relations with the Soviet Union has some political implications. Relations with Japan are very important, but the actual relationship is probably more economic and less political (diplomatic). Because at this time, the United States is in a hurry to seek economic balance, and if the surplus heavy industrial goods can be sold in the Soviet Union, it is also a way to restore prosperity. Although the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan is said to be successful, it is only the initial construction. After that, it will undoubtedly devote itself to domestic development. Therefore, even if the United States and the Soviet Union resume diplomatic relations, even if the rift between Japan and the Soviet Union deepens, it will have an impact on Japan's invasion, but it still cannot stop the Japanese army's rampage and reduce its military adventurous advance. It is feared that it will become even more violent and reckless.

Wang Jingwei Arrived in Nanjing Yesterday 18

Reported at the Memorial Week of the Central Party Headquarters

The only way out is resistance, and we must pay attention to the ability to resist

The Central Government Held an Important Meeting

Nanjing: President Wang, Vice President Song, along with Chu Minyi, Zeng Zhongming, Chen Gongbo, Tang Youren, Gan Naiguang, Shi Qingyang, Bai Yunti, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Bijun, Liang Hancao, and others arrived in Nanjing at 7:45 am on the 20th. Song got off the train at Hepingmen, while Wang and others got off the train at Xiaguan. Chairman Lin sent Civil Service Director Wei Huai as his representative to welcome them at the station. In addition, Tang Shengzhi, Ye Chucang, Chen Shaokuan, Zhang Ji, He Yaozu, Gu Zhenglun, Chen Zhuo, Wang Luyi, Chen Shuren, Ke Xing'e, Gu Zhenggang, and representatives from various agencies, numbering several hundred, were at the station to welcome them. After Wang got off the train, he immediately took a car to the Central Party Headquarters to attend the Memorial Week report. (Twentieth Day Central News Agency Electric Report)

Nanjing: After attending the Memorial Week, President Wang returned to the official residence of the Ministry of Railways to rest. At 10:00, he attended an important meeting held by the Central Government. Chairman Lin, Yu Youren, Ju Zheng, Dai Chuanxian, Ye Chucang, Zhang Ji, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Shaokuan, Luo Wengan, and others attended. The meeting adjourned at noon. Chu Minyi said that Wang's diabetes was slightly more serious than when he was in Singapore. Whether he will resume his position as President of the Executive Yuan depends on his physical strength. However, regardless of whether he resumes his post or not, he will definitely be responsible to the Central Government. Whether Wang will go to Baoding to meet Chiang or Chiang will return to Nanjing is still undecided. (Twentieth Day Central News Agency Electric Report)

Nanjing: At 10:00 am on the 20th, the Central Party Headquarters held an important meeting. Wang Jingwei, Song Ziwen, and various important figures in the Central Government in Nanjing attended. It is reported that there were secret discussions on national defense, foreign affairs, and other issues. (Twentieth Day Special Dispatch)

Nanjing: The Central Party Headquarters held a memorial week for the Premier at 9:00 am on the 20th. Chairman Lin, Yu Youren, Ju Zheng, and others participated. President Wang reported, the original text said: Chairman, fellow comrades, I took the train this morning to participate in the Memorial Week. I originally wanted to listen to the speeches of the Chairman and fellow comrades, but the Chairman wanted me to say a few words. Although I was not prepared, the Chairman's intention was probably because I had been out for a few months and now I have returned, giving me some opportunities to meet with fellow comrades. So I had to say a few words. Recalling a few months ago, the Central Government, considering that my illness was serious, gave me a few months' vacation to go to Europe for treatment. I am sincerely grateful for the Central Government's kindness. But when this country is in crisis and existence is at stake, fellow comrades are working hard and striving hard, while I am leisurely lying in bed, which is really uneasy. When the bad news of Shanhaiguan came, I had to return to the country in a hurry before my illness was cured. On the way, I received the bad news of the fall of Rehe, which made me even more worried. Then I got the news that Comrade Chiang Kai-shek went north to supervise the army, and the soldiers of all fronts worked together to support the front line. I was a little comforted by the sorrow and indignation. Considering the hard work and sacrifice of the soldiers on the front line and the difficult cooperation of the comrades of the Central Government, I was infinitely terrified from comfort. I would like to pay my deepest respect to the soldiers on the front line and the comrades of the Central Government. What do I want to say? To this day, there is nothing to say except the word resistance. Of course, resistance and negotiation go hand in hand, but the fundamental principle for dealing with the current situation must first be resistance, and then negotiation. The recent resolution of the League of Nations shows that Japan is an aggressor and China is the victim of aggression. The justice of the world has not been completely lost. This is the result of negotiation, that is, the result of resistance. From today onwards, the more effective the resistance, the more hopeful the negotiation. Otherwise, there is no negotiation to speak of. Therefore, our only way out today is resistance. Speaking of resistance, it seems to contain a lot of meaning. First of all, we must have the determination to resist, and secondly, we must have the ability to resist. Today, no one in China should not have the determination to resist. This is self-evident. Now

Photo of President Wang Arriving in Beijing 19

What needs to be said is only the ability to resist. What is the ability to resist? The most obvious is military force. But where does military force come from? First of all, materially speaking, our weapons are very scarce. This is well known. Guns, cannons, ammunition, and all military equipment are not as good as the enemy's. Our soldiers on the front line are almost flesh and blood, fighting the enemy's scientific weapons. To talk about strengthening the ability to resist, the first is to strengthen weapons. This is beyond doubt. But where do weapons come from? Is the ability to resist limited to weapons materially? China claims to be a country based on agriculture, but according to the customs figures of last year, the total value of grain imports reached 300 million taels. We, China, a country based on agriculture, have to spend 300 million taels every year to buy foreign grain. Without these grain imports, the Chinese people would starve to death. If they starve to death, even if they have weapons, they will not be able to fight. It can be seen that the ability to resist is not limited to weapons materially. The poor Chinese have to spend 300 million taels to buy grain to avoid starvation. Then where is the spare money to manufacture weapons or even buy weapons? It can be seen that the ability to resist must also take into account all aspects materially. Modern countries usually focus on production and develop the productive capacity of the people. When it comes to war, they use the productive capacity of the people as much as possible for the resistance of military force. Therefore, the greater the productive capacity of the people, the greater the resistance of military force. Taking Russia during the European War as an example, it did not focus on the productive capacity of the people at ordinary times, but only on the strengthening of military force. Therefore, it was defeated when it fought against Germany. Taking the United States as an example, although it did not pay much attention to military preparations at ordinary times, because the productive capacity of the people was sufficient, it immediately sent 2 million troops and all kinds of military supplies, like mountains and seas, to Europe, so that the Allied countries won the final victory. From this, it can be seen that if you want to strengthen military force, you must not do without strengthening the productive capacity of the people. How can we make the productive capacity of the people sufficient? At least, at least, the people should live and work in peace, and the lives, property, and freedom of the people should be guaranteed. It can be seen that if you don't talk about resistance, it is already over, if you don't talk about the ability to resist, it is already over. If you talk about it, you will know that the cultivation of the ability to resist is not just a military issue, but a political issue and a social issue. The above is only about the material aspect. In fact, the ability to resist is by no means limited to the material aspect. Pay attention to the spiritual and organizational aspects at the same time. The ancients said that the past is not to be blamed, but the experience of the past is a teacher for the future. We may as well give one example. The fall of Chengde was the result of the non-resistance of Tang Yulin's troops. Tang Yulin's troops generally had guns, cannons, and all the necessary armaments. But why didn't they resist? This is due to the reason of planting opium. It is impossible to expect someone who plants opium to resist. The generals are like this, and the army is naturally like this. As for the people, they are forced to plant opium and forced to eat opium every day. Even if they want to resist, they really can't. It is also impossible to expect them to resist and to resist for a long time. Fellow comrades already know that the same army, the same guns, the same clothes, those who have received national education and have the spirit of the National Revolutionary Army must have a stronger resistance ability. On the contrary, those who have not received national education and do not have the spirit of the National Revolutionary Army must have a weaker resistance ability. We have seen many times that those who are inferior to others materially but superior in spirit have won victory, and we have never seen those who are inferior in spirit but superior materially win victory. This is true for military affairs, and it is also true for other things. Therefore, from the material aspect, from the spiritual aspect, and from the organizational aspect, the so-called ability to resist is by no means just a military issue, but also a political issue and a social issue. So, in summary, to strengthen the ability to resist, we must think of various ways from the political and social aspects, first strengthen the productive capacity of the people, and then think of various ways to make the productive capacity of the people applicable to military force. Therefore, the biggest problem today is not just the problem of resisting Japan, but the problem of the survival of the Chinese nation. The Chinese nation must have the self-consciousness to seek survival and possess the conditions for survival before it can resist Japan. Therefore, we today must not only have the determination to resist, but also have the ability to resist. Without the determination to resist, the country will perish. Without the ability to resist, the country will also perish. Speaking of this, the tragic scene of the country's perishing three hundred years ago is as if it is in front of us. When Xiong Tingbi and Yuan Chonghuan were confronting Manchuria in Liaodong, the Chinese scholar-officials, the unscrupulous ones, need not be said. The conscientious ones, known as gentlemen, were also empty and sang a strong high tune. Arguing for peace was immediately said to be colluding with the enemy and selling the country. Arguing for war, there were soldiers but no pay, and generals but no soldiers. When the great enemy was in front of us, there was no other way but to die for the country. These people only had the determination to resist, but did not have the ability to resist. The result of the country's perishing is heartbreaking to think about. We must never repeat this mistake today. The insufficient ability to resist in China today is undoubtedly undeniable. But with the size of China and the population of 400 million, to say that there are no conditions for resistance in terms of material, spirit, and organization is really self-defeating. We must know that the people do not lack the productive capacity, but they are not well cultivated, and even destroyed instead. Therefore, the productive capacity of the people cannot be developed. If we can pay attention to cultivating the productive capacity of the people and pay attention to making the productive capacity of the people applicable to military force, then resistance is not without certainty, and long-term resistance is not without hope. I read various resolutions of the Third Plenary Session while I was ill, and I know that the Third Plenary Session has already instructed these guidelines to comrades and the general public. What is necessary today is not to speak, but to practice, especially to practice urgently. The ancients said that to reward good and punish evil can destroy a country. It is not that to reward good and punish evil can destroy a country, but that to reward good and not use it, and to punish evil and not remove it, is why a country is destroyed. To reward good and punish evil is to speak, to reward good and be able to use it, and to punish evil and be able to remove it is to practice. Thinking of this, I am really filled with grief. Why can't China cultivate the productive capacity of the people? Why can't the productive capacity of the people be applied to military force? It is all because there are many evil people who sabotage and obstruct it. Of course, I know that when the Central Government is resisting Japan, it does not have the spare energy to eliminate these evil people, but the Central Government must not have a compromising mind to condone these evil people. At least, at least, it should clearly state their crimes and abandon them with the people of the country. In this way, people with one heart and one mind will unite to bear the current difficulties. As for those evil people, let them prepare to be slaves to the country. Whether to reward good and be able to use it or to punish evil and be able to remove it is a matter of fact, but to reward good and be sure to use it, and to punish evil and be sure to remove it, is a matter of will. If the will is firm, it is not difficult to gradually become a fact. Otherwise, even the will is gone, and it will only become empty words. I think that the Central Government must not have scruples and make it real, so that those who exploit the people to enrich themselves and divide the country for their own selfish interests will gradually be unable to stand in China, and then they will be able to cultivate the productive capacity of the people and make the productive capacity of the people applicable to military force. The country is in a critical state of survival. What I just said seems too far away, but it seems that there is no more practical way. We can only do this. We must not only not calculate success or failure, but also not calculate my death. We can only prepare to die on the battlefield instead of dying in bed. Even if we cannot save the country from disaster in our lifetime, we must always find a way out for the Chinese people who die after us, so that they can cultivate productive capacity and apply productive capacity to military force, so as to achieve the purpose of resistance and seek the survival of the Chinese nation. (Central News Agency Electric Report on the 22nd)

Nanjing: Wang Zhaoming returned to Beijing on the morning of the 20th to attend the Central Memorial Report, and returned to the Ministry of Railways' official residence to rest. At 10:00, he went to the Central Party Headquarters again to convene an important meeting. Lin Sen, Yu Youren, Dai Chuanxian, Ju Zheng, Ye Chucang, Luo Wengan, Chen Shaokuan, Chen Guofu, Zhang Ji, Chen Shuren, and more than 20 others participated. The meeting adjourned at noon, and Wang returned to his residence for lunch. At 1:00 pm, Tang Shengzhi, Zeng Zhongming, Peng Xuepei, and the heads of various ministries and commissions visited him. Foreign Minister Luo also visited him at 2:00 pm and discussed foreign affairs issues until 2:00 pm before leaving. According to Wang's words to reporters, he has not yet recovered from his illness, and he still intends to ask the Central Government to have Song Zhen replace him as President of the Executive Yuan. It is undecided whether he will go to Baoding to meet Chiang. At present, there is only concentration of strength and unity to resist Japan. There is no other opinion to say. Zeng Zhongming also told reporters that Wang has not recovered from his illness and still needs to see a doctor. If he resumes his position as President of the Executive Yuan at this time, it is feared that the symptoms will worsen again. If he then retires again, it will inevitably cause criticism from the outside world. Therefore, Wang is determined not to resume his position as President of the Executive Yuan. Wang will be responsible for presiding over major plans in the Central Government in the future. Chu Minyi also told reporters that Wang's diabetes is more serious than when he was in Singapore. Whether he will resume his post depends on his physical strength. According to another report, Wang needs to meet and discuss major national plans with Chiang. The issue of resuming his post will be completely decided after the meeting with Chiang. (Central News Agency Electric Report on the 20th)

Yu Youren Reported

Absolutely Will Not Compromise With the Enemy

Thinking of the continuous domestic wars of the past 20 years, it is really unfair to the heroic soldiers who have only encountered the real enemy today. Mussolini's Initiative 21

European Quadruple Cooperation

Aims to Enhance the Spirit of the Kellogg-Briand Pact for Lasting World Peace. MacDonald Departs Yesterday via Paris to Return Home. Italian Plan Delivered to French and German Ambassadors for Consultation.

Rome - A public statement was released today, regarding the talks held last night and this afternoon between British Prime Minister MacDonald, Foreign Secretary Simon, and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. It stated that after discussing the general situation, the British and Italian authorities studied a plan to seek understanding on major political issues. This plan was initiated by Mussolini, its purpose being to gain the cooperation of the Western powers of Britain, France, Italy, and Germany to enhance the spirit of the Kellogg-Briand Pact, issue a declaration renouncing the use of force, and seek lasting peace in Europe and the world.

Rome - British and Italian sides are unwilling to comment further on the precise meaning of the aforementioned joint British-Italian statement. However, it is understood that Mussolini's initiative, which seeks understanding among the four powers, has already been conveyed to the French and German ambassadors stationed in Italy. Mutual consultations among the four powers will be handled by the heads of government, hoping to resolve major issues that could trigger significant conflicts in Europe at any time. It is reported that this plan is merely a method of contact and does not contain specific measures for resolving these issues. The revision of treaties currently occupies a large part of the discussions between the British and French authorities, while disarmament has barely been discussed. At 6:30 PM tonight, the British Prime Minister and Foreign Secretary paid a visit to the Pope, talking for 35 minutes. The British delegation is scheduled to depart for London tomorrow afternoon, with a brief stopover in Paris. (Reuters, 19th)

Paris - British Prime Minister MacDonald and Foreign Secretary Simon are expected to arrive in Paris at 10:00 AM tomorrow. They will have lunch with French Prime Minister Daladier and Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour at the British Embassy. At that time, British-French talks will begin. The British delegation is scheduled to return to London on Wednesday to participate in the debate on foreign affairs in the House of Commons. The debate in the House will involve not only the Sino-Japanese dispute but also the talks in Geneva, Paris, and Rome. (Reuters, 20th)

Alignment of British Views

Rome - British Prime Minister MacDonald received reporters today, stating that regarding the conversation with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini recorded in last night's statement, no additions or speculations should be made. The discussions mainly concerned the situation in Europe and various issues and were of an exchange of information nature. He and the Italian Prime Minister will continue to cooperate to find a solution acceptable to all parties, ensuring peace in Europe for at least thirty years. The British Prime Minister did not say, "I feel that the entire atmosphere of Rome has undergone a spiritual change." The characteristic of the talks between the heads of state of the two countries was the alignment of their views. Both sides are now considering a method to achieve understanding on major political issues, broadly similar to the plan Mussolini expressed in his speech in Turin last October, which closely aligns with the British viewpoint. As for the phrase "no use of force" in the statement, it was already mentioned in the five-power agreement of December 11 last year, which requested Germany to rejoin the Disarmament Conference. Clause 3 of the agreement states that the British, French, German, and Italian governments are prepared to join the solemn declaration made by European countries, that under no circumstances should any country rely on the use of force to resolve current or future disputes among the signatories. (Reuters, 20th)

Prime Minister MacDonald's Remarks Before Leaving Italy 22

Rome - British Prime Minister MacDonald's personal efforts in Geneva and Rome to salvage the Disarmament Conference have led him to believe that a general European agreement can be reached. Before departing for Paris, MacDonald told a Reuters reporter that now is the time to seize practical opportunities rather than engage in fantasies. The most important thing now is to seek a compromise between France and Germany. MacDonald also said that rumors of an agreement already being in place are unfounded. (Reuters, 20th)

Hungary and Italy Reach Political Understanding 23

Rome - The Hungarian Foreign Minister stated to reporters today that after meeting with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, he firmly believes that Hungary's foreign policy inclination towards the East in 1927 and its close understanding with Italy are entirely appropriate and correct, and can be called an important asset in the restructuring of European politics. (Guomin News Agency, 19th)

Rome - Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, during his meeting with British Prime Minister MacDonald and Foreign Secretary Simon, proposed that Italy, Britain, France, and Germany sign a new peace pact to maintain peace in Europe. This proposal is now being studied by the four countries. If all agree, it will be signed in Rome with a solemn ceremony. Today, the Italian Prime Minister and British officials met for a long time at the British Embassy, explaining the details of his plan. Afterwards, a public statement was issued stating that after the leaders of the two countries exchanged detailed opinions on the overall situation, they studied Prime Minister Mussolini's proposed plan for understanding on larger political issues, hoping to gain the cooperative efforts of the four major Western powers to enhance the spirit of the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the declaration renouncing the use of force, and to promote lasting peace in Europe and the world. The details of Mussolini's plan have not yet been released, but it is said to share many similarities with MacDonald's previous plan. If the new pact is established, it will be called the Four-Power Pact for Maintaining European Peace. The first chapter will identify the participating countries, followed by a summary of the principles of the Kellogg-Briand Pact, adding sanctions for those who attempt to incite armed conflict. It is also rumored that French Prime Minister Daladier and German Chancellor Hitler will be invited to Rome soon for similar discussions. Once all four countries agree to this proposal, the Italian government will send representatives from the three countries to Rome to formally sign the new pact, which will be named the Mussolini Pact or the Rome Pact. (Guomin News Agency, 19th)

Not Incompatible with the League of Nations 24

Rome - The most important point in the British-Italian talks is that Mussolini put forward a completely unknown plan. The only thing that has been discussed so far is the preface to this plan. This plan has already been communicated to the French government before the meeting. What the British cabinet members will discuss with the French authorities after arriving in Paris next Tuesday is this plan, but with British opinions added. Mussolini's intention is to have the four major powers preside over Europe. Judging from yesterday's meeting, it can be seen that Mussolini's intention is not incompatible with the nature of the League of Nations. Therefore, the main part of the Italian plan can be used to reform the international organization and make it more solid. Since Japan left Geneva, this matter is easier to handle because the permanent members of the Executive Council are only four countries, and these four countries are the four major powers referred to in the Italian plan. As for the other countries, the British cabinet members do not intend to exclude them from participation, but if the major powers can reach a compromise first, the other countries will be more likely to agree. In addition, Britain has a strong reaction to German Chancellor Hitler's violence. The Italian Prime Minister is well aware of this, so he specially advised Germany with a friendly attitude to reassure Britain. (Havas News Agency, 19th)

Rome - British Prime Minister MacDonald and his daughter departed for Paris at 12:15 PM today. Those seeing them off at the station included Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Suvich, British Ambassador to Italy Sir Graham and his wife, and French Ambassador to Italy Jouvenel. British Foreign Secretary Simon flew to Genoa. (Havas News Agency, 20th)

Speculations by French Newspaper Reporters 25

Paris - The Times correspondent in Rome commented on the British-Italian talks, saying that Mussolini and MacDonald have agreed to lead Europe into a trend dominated by the four major powers, excluding all countries that have consistently supported French policy. In Rome, a speculation is increasingly believed that MacDonald is mediating, persuading Mussolini to advise German Chancellor Hitler to exercise restraint and adopt a peaceful attitude. However, Germans in Rome fear that Mussolini is secretly beginning to get closer to France without informing Berlin. The rumor that German Chancellor Hitler will visit Rome at the end of this month or the beginning of next month originated from this. In addition, some people deliberately spread rumors that Hungarian Foreign Minister Kánya will meet with MacDonald specifically regarding the Hungarian issue. Others say that MacDonald has suggested consolidating the Locarno Treaty to allow France to agree to substantial disarmament.

(Havas News Agency, 19th)

British New Disarmament Plan 26

Japan Maintains Opposing Stance

Tokyo - The Japanese Navy Department still opposes the British new disarmament proposal, stating that while the plan may be needed in Europe, Japan cannot accept any disarmament proposals in the face of the urgent situation in the Far East. (Hualian News Agency, 20th)

Tokyo - As a result of the Japanese naval authorities considering the attitude of the Japanese Navy towards British Prime Minister MacDonald's disarmament plan, the following items were decided, and a telegram was sent to the Japanese delegation in Geneva to prepare for submission to the General Disarmament Committee: (1) Japan does not recognize the necessity of the security guarantee issue. (2) Japan advocates disclosing the holdings stipulated in the Washington and London Treaties for naval armaments, therefore opposing the convocation of the 1935 World Naval Conference. (3) Japan reserves its opinion on whether to support or oppose the issues of the complete abolition of aircraft carriers and the land and sea military strength until the two issues are decided. (4) Japan opposes limiting the weight of aircraft to three tons. (5) The original proposal limits the maximum number of aircraft for Britain, France, Italy, and Japan to 500 each, but Japan expresses opposition before the above issues are resolved. (6) The Japanese Navy requests the Disarmament Conference to review the Japanese disarmament proposal submitted last year. (Japan United News Agency, 20th)

Jinan

There are indigenous people in Ming Dynasty clothing who often come out of the mountains to exchange medicine for goods. Roosevelt's New Writings 51

Elaborating Political Views in Detail

New York, 19th (Havas) - President Roosevelt's new book, titled "Looking Forward," serves to publish his political and economic views, with particular emphasis on the League of Nations and the US financial situation. Roosevelt stated, "While we are striving to improve our economic position, such improvements are difficult to sustain if the world's resources are not more fairly distributed." Regarding the world's experience of panic, the President said he hoped that all suffering countries could make concessions to overcome difficulties and avoid commercial stagnation. Roosevelt reiterated that countries worldwide should send representatives to a conference on commercial issues, and the United States would participate. However, this should not be interpreted as the United States joining the League of Nations, as even with US membership, it could not help the world avoid war. International difficulties, even with US participation, could not be resolved according to the main ideas underlying US policy. The League of Nations has not developed along the lines anticipated by its founders; its major member states would rather sacrifice large sums of money to engage in armaments than use it to develop commerce, balance budgets, or fulfill their contracts. Roosevelt also said that people use their bank deposits for speculation, and such speculation is encouraged by the government. He advocates stopping this speculation and finding ways to discourage people from engaging in it. He firmly believes that economic thinking will soon undergo fundamental changes. In the future, we will focus on the interests of consumers, not just producers.

Reasons for Russia Arresting British Nationals 54

It should be noted that water turbines are large objects, and millions of liters of water flow through them every day. Even if someone put sand or acid into the car, it would be washed away by the water and would not damage the machine parts. This matter must be a misunderstanding.

Unprecedented Fierce Battle at Luowenyu 60

Enemy Changes Offensive Strategy After Defeat at Xifeng, Our Song Unit Fights Bravely to Break Through Enemy's Second Line of Defense, Great Sword's Divine Power Captures Three Enemy Commanders Alive

Beiping Correspondence - The enemy's attacking force in Rehe totals seven brigades. The Motegi Cavalry Brigade has been defeated by Sun Dianying. The Hattori and Suzuki brigades were eliminated by Song Zheyuan. Four brigades are distributed in Chifeng, Chengde, Rexi, and the various passes of the Great Wall, and their forces are insufficient for distribution. It is reported that a division has been transferred from inside the Pass to reinforce them, having landed in Dalian and heading to Rehe for combat. Meanwhile, Commander Mutō has transferred the Fifth Regiment of the Guyi First Brigade and the Thirty-first Regiment of the Hayakawa Stop Brigade from Chengde, combined with the elite of the cavalry artillery, totaling approximately 5,000 men, to launch a fierce assault on Malanguan and Luowenyu from the Banbishan and Foye Ridge areas, in an attempt to retaliate. Therefore, along the Luowenyu line, the Japanese army launched a general offensive on Sancha on the morning of the 17th with heavy troops, and the intensity of the artillery fire was unprecedented. According to Xiao Zhenying, a member of the Military Commission who returned to Beiping from the front, the fierce battle unfolded as follows: The Japanese troops attacking Rehe originally planned to break through Xifengkou and Gubeikou, attempting to occupy the various passes of the Great Wall. The Japanese Hattori Brigade attacked Xifengkou, and our Zhao Dengyu Brigade launched a night attack on the 10th, eliminating the enemy. The Japanese army changed its strategy, transferring the main force from Chengde to launch a fierce attack on Luowenyu. At 8:30 this morning (17th), the Japanese army launched a general offensive on Sancha Mountain with a brigade. Most of the Japanese artillery bombarded the mountain with volley fire. Two companies of our infantry defending the mountain fought bravely under the enemy's fierce artillery fire. From morning to noon, the enemy fired over 500 shells. Our Division Commander Liu Ruming personally led the pistol battalion to reinforce and dispatched a regiment along the mountain path to attack from both sides. At 1:00 PM, our army attacked into the enemy's defense line. Both sides engaged in close combat, using guns, bayonets, and broadswords in hand-to-hand combat. The Japanese soldiers were defeated and retreated across the line. Commander Song learned of the tense situation in Luowenyu in a certain location and rushed to the front line from a certain location. More than 40 Japanese airplanes strongly bombed our positions, and the sound of booming artillery could be heard throughout Zunhua and Su County. At 2:00 PM, I separated from Commander Song and returned to Shijiazhuang by car. Commander Song notified the Shijiazhuang telephone bureau in advance to invite me to talk. Commander Song reported on the phone that our army had attacked into the enemy's second line of defense and captured three Japanese commanders alive. Currently, they are engaged in fierce fighting in the second line of defense. Enemy troops were discovered in Dongjiakou yesterday morning (16th) and have been repelled. During this time, the Japanese army at Xifengkou launched a fierce attack on the defense line. At that time, Wan's troops retreated. As soon as our army arrived at the defense line, Japanese armored vehicles and tanks charged. One of our battalions charged bravely, and no one survived. On the night of the 10th, our Brigade Commander Zhao Dengyu personally led his troops in a night attack, wielding his sword and killing many Japanese soldiers. The sword was already bent and has been brought back to Beiping by the inspection team from the Beida front line and will be displayed at the museum. Currently, the officers and soldiers at the front line have been awake for seven days and nights, enduring hardships. Soldiers climb mountains and run at night, and their shoes have been worn out, exposing their toes. When enemy planes come, our army lies hidden in the mountains. Many wounded soldiers were left at the front line, but transportation is difficult due to a lack of cars. After returning to Beiping, I will visit Minister He tomorrow (18th) and go to Baoding to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek tomorrow night to report everything.

Another report stated that the enemy who invaded our Xifengkou, after being severely attacked by our Song Zheyuan's troops for days, dare not attack our position again. Considering this to be the first extraordinary shame and humiliation suffered by Japan since the Meiji military training, the punishment received can be imagined. According to a certain staff officer who returned to Beiping from the front line, the reasons for Song's unit's victory are roughly three points: (1) The general's determination is firm. After Song's troops arrived at the front line, he gathered his troops and stated generously: "The enemy is pressing forward step by step, and it has reached its limit. Without strength, there is no justice. To resist, you must first have determination. Yue Wumu said, 'Eat the flesh of the barbarians while hungry, and drink the blood of the Huns when thirsty.' This is the time. If we meet the enemy, we must have the determination to advance without retreat and die." He personally wrote these eight characters to inform his subordinates. (2) Unified command and cooperation. At the beginning of the war, Song ordered Feng and Zhang's divisions to each draw a brigade to encircle the enemy's rear and launch simultaneous attacks. All units were able to obey orders and bravely advance without delay, so they could achieve their goals. (3) Soldiers are brave. The soldiers of this unit are well-trained, and the general's command is appropriate, so they can sacrifice themselves and kill many enemies. (18th)

Song Zheyuan 61

Achievements in Governing Chahar

Promoting Water Conservancy, Encouraging Well-Drilling. Emphasizing Culture, Rectifying Transportation. Pacifying the People, Searching for Bandits

Beiping Correspondence - Since the fall of Rehe and the alarm in North China, Song Zheyuan, who has repeatedly defeated the Japanese army, has commanded his troops to bravely kill the enemy, greatly boosting his prestige. We already know Song's bravery in governing the army. Yesterday, I met a certain gentleman who is currently the secretary of the Chahar Provincial Government, who spoke of Song's achievements since taking office as Chairman of Chahar. Although the time has been very short, his achievements are worth mentioning. Here is a summary of the main points:

Encouraging Well-Drilling 62

Chahar Province is high and has few rivers. Whenever there is a lack of rainfall, the suffering of drought is immediately felt. Not only is there no water for irrigation, but even garden vegetables are often left to wither. Even drinking water is insufficient, and there is not a well to be seen for three or five miles. This situation is even worse in the Mongolian banner areas. After Song arrived in Chahar, he ordered the Construction Department to vigorously advocate well-drilling, hoping to conquer nature with manpower and create great benefits for agriculture. The measures are: (1) County chiefs, directors of construction bureaus, and district and village chiefs are responsible for encouraging people to drill wells. The number of newly drilled wells in their respective jurisdictions is the most important standard for their performance evaluation. (2) Those who vigorously promote encouragement and people who voluntarily drill wells will be rewarded. (3) Rewards are divided into four types: recording merits, issuing commendations, awarding plaques, and medals. Therefore, the number of newly drilled wells recently is very large.

Rectifying Transportation 63

Chahar's transportation industry has gradually developed in recent years. Song paid more attention to management, so provincial and county highways were built in sequence, and roads for motor vehicles were also built. The dredging of river channels and the addition of bridges are also proceeding in order. Currently, long-distance telephones within the province have been vigorously reorganized, which is much more efficient than in the past.

Searching for Bandits 64

The bandits in Inner Mongolia have long been famous. In the Chahar-Suiyuan area for over ten years, people have been killed, raped, and abducted by bandits every day. After the K Army was withdrawn due to the outbreak of war last year, bandits took the opportunity to carry out large-scale activities, gathering thousands of people, wreaking havoc across the four borders, breaking cities and occupying land. In addition, there have been frequent droughts, floods, frosts, and hailstorms in recent years, and many people have been forced by the environment to become bandits. After Song entered Chahar, he sent teams to suppress and capture bandits, repeatedly capturing ringleaders, such as Black Face Yao San and Ma Shangbian, who were all experts in the field. They were successively arrested, either brought to justice or pacified and returned to civilization. Combining both force and leniency, and using it properly, if given time, it should not be difficult to completely eliminate the bandits and allow good people to live in peace.

Han Fuqu 65

Goes to Baoding to Meet Chiang

Chiang Sends Jiang Bocheng to Jinan to Invite Him - Special Train Passes Through Beiping to Baoding

Jinan Correspondence - Chiang Kai-shek's representative, Jiang Bocheng, arrived in Jinan from Tianjin at 9:00 AM on the 18th because he had important business to discuss with Shandong Province Chairman Han Fuqu. Province Chairman Han Fuqu, Secretary-General Zhang Shaotang, Civil Affairs Director Li Shuchun, and others all went to the station to welcome him. After Jiang got off the train and exchanged pleasantries with the greeters, he went to the Jiaoji Hotel for talks. According to Jiang's account of his mission to Jinan, this trip was undertaken on the order of Chairman Chiang to invite Chairman Han to go to Baoding in order to discuss national plans with Chairman Chiang. He also said that he had originally gone to the Beining Line from Beiping at 2:30 PM the day before (16th) to comfort the troops. He returned to Beidaihe early yesterday (17th) and returned to Tianjin with Pang Bingxun that night. Pang went to Baoding to meet Chairman Chiang, and he came to Jinan to meet Chairman Han and had already negotiated the trip to Baoding. Set off tonight (18th). On the front lines, our army has repeatedly won victories. Xifengkou, Gubeikou, Lengkou, Dalinghe, and Shihe have all taken the upper hand, and morale is very high. There is no movement in the direction of Yu Pass. After Zhang Hanqing resigned from the Military Commission branch in Beiping, Minister He took over. The staff has not changed. Office Director Rong Zhen resigned due to illness and has been replaced by Bao Wen. The rumor that I will take over as Office Director is absolutely untrue. Public affairs are not a matter for one person. We should now strive to eliminate the ills of "one emperor, one courtier."

Since Han Fuqu was invited by Chiang Bocheng on orders and negotiated the trip north with Chiang, he immediately ordered Transport Director Guan Shiqian to prepare the train and telegraphed 20th Division Commander Sun Tongxuan and 29th Division Commander Cao Fulin to come to Jinan to discuss the province's defense. Sun and Cao arrived on the 18th from their defense stations, and Han held a meeting in the Provincial Government. In addition to the two division commanders Sun and Cao, 22nd Division Commander Gu Liangmin, Handgun Brigade Commander Wu Huawen, Headquarters Chief of Staff Liu Shuxiang, and all section chiefs, Civil Affairs Director Li Shuchun, Finance Director Wang Xiangrong, Provincial Government Secretary-General He Shaotang, and others attended. Han instructed them to carefully maintain the province's defense. Headquarters affairs were entrusted to Gu Liangmin and Liu Shuxiang for acting on their behalf, and Provincial Government affairs were entrusted to Li Shuchun and Zhang Shaotang for acting on their behalf. If there is an emergency, telegraph at any time for instructions. He also ordered Councilor Zhang Lian, Yao Yijia, Zhang Shouqian, Bureau Chief Niu Zhao, Deputy Director Meng Guangshan, Head of the Reception Department Zhang Xichen, Han Huancen, Section Chief of the Staff Department Jiang Renchun, and Director of the Telegraph Office, etc. to accompany him. Other departments also sent staff for consultation. One radio station and two companies of guards were also taken. At 6:00 PM, the special train was also prepared, with five first-class passenger cars, eight covered cars, six Taishan Team armored cars, one third-class car, and one locomotive at each end, a total of twenty-two carriages. At 7:00 PM, the accompanying guards began to board the train. At 10:00 PM, Han also arrived at the station. At 10:30 PM, Jiang Bocheng arrived. All the party, government, and military leaders all went to the station to see him off. Chairman Ge Guangting of the Jiaoji Railway Committee also went to Baoding to meet Chiang.

Han told reporters at the station about his mission to the north, saying that Chairman Chiang had sent General Counselor Jiang (Bocheng) to Jinan to convey his intention, ordering him to go to Baoding. There was also a telegram today, although he did not specify what was happening, but it was not known to be an instruction on resisting Japan and defending against insults. However, the coastal defense of Shandong is important, and it is probably not possible to order the Shandong team to go north. It was originally intended to go directly from Jinan to Baoding without going to Beiping, but Minister He had a telegram summoning him, so it was decided to go to Beiping first, stay for one day, and then go to Baoding, returning to Jinan in at most six days. I originally intended to go to Beijing this month to meet with Chairman Chiang and Minister He to report on the province's military affairs and ask for instructions on everything. Because of the Yuguan incident, Chairman Chiang ordered me to sit in Jinan, so I could not go. As the Rehe war began and North China became tense, Shandong's defense was also very important. Without orders, I dare not leave without authorization, so I first sent Commissioner Zhang (Yue) to Baoding to ask for instructions. Now that I have been ordered to go, I should leave immediately. I will obey all orders from the central government and Chairman Chiang. At 11:30 PM, he shook hands with the farewell party and boarded the train to go north. (19th)

Songjiang 66

Continued News on the Tenant's Suicide Case

Yesterday, Dong Qingyu's family in the neighborhood suddenly had a tenant, Wang Heshang, from Qingpu, commit suicide by cutting his throat. For a while, discussions were buzzing with different opinions about the cause of the suicide. After receiving the report, the County Court Prosecutor's Office immediately sent Prosecutor Zhu Zonghai, along with bailiffs and police, to investigate. The investigation confirmed that the knife wound was on the right side of the neck, a vital point, which caused death. The coroner filled out the death certificate and took Dong Qingyu back for investigation, then issued a warrant for his arrest. It is reported that the deceased's wife and children heard the news and came to Songjiang, wailing loudly over the body. After mediation by Dong's family, it is said that Dong's family paid 60 yuan in compensation. The family then claimed the body and hired a boat to take it home for burial. It is said that the compensation was advertised as 60 yuan, but there were other conditions within it. The family of the deceased has already solved the legal problem, but it may not be resolved quickly for a while.

Suzhou 67

Money Industry Opposes Business Tax

According to the Wu County Money Industry Association's letter to the Wu County Chamber of Commerce, the Business Tax Bureau is forcing them to fill out repeated declarations, which is considered to be an exploitation of merchants, and has presented three reasons: (1) The commerce of Suzhou is declining. Those in power should be trying to rescue it and cannot bear to impose taxes. (2) Suzhou and Shanghai are close neighbors. Shanghai has no tax. The same business is extremely unfair. (3) The Bank of China has no tax. The money industry alone bears a heavy tax. It is inevitable to destroy the money industry. At this time when the abolition of taels and the change of yuan is imminent, there is no way to survive, so they risked speaking out, etc. After receiving the letter, the Chamber of Commerce forwarded it to the Suzhou Finance Department on the 20th to ask for instructions.

County Party Headquarters Ceases Activities 68

Wu County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee member Zhang Zongmin, etc., was accused by party member Gu Baiyu and others to the Provincial Party Headquarters of accepting bribes, shielding gambling and drugs, stealing and selling enemy goods, and using private individuals. After the Provincial Party Headquarters sent Mr. Wang to Suzhou for investigation, it ordered the association to cease its activities and sent Li Junliang to temporarily take custody.

Wuxi 69

Carelessness at Salad Oil Factory

Director X of the Tongyuan Rice Shop under the Gongyun Bridge outside the North Gate secretly set up a Ronghu Salad Oil Refinery behind Zhang Alley opposite the Lixin Cloth Factory on Huishang Bridge. The business was developing well. But at about 11:00 AM yesterday (21st), the factory suddenly caught fire. Because of the accumulation of kerosene, it was impossible to extinguish it. Fire brigades from nearby sections rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm. It had already burned the salad oil and kerosene tanks. The barrels caught fire and exploded, with lead sheets flying everywhere, making it difficult for the firefighters to rescue. It was not extinguished until about 1:00 PM. In addition to the factory building being burned down, more than ten "shun" of salad oil and more than 100 boxes of kerosene were burned, with a total loss of approximately 3,000 yuan.

Local News 70

Yesterday's Review

Model of Sun Yat-sen's Statue

Opening Ceremony on November 12, Construction Costing a Total of 12,000 Yuan

Since the model of Sun Yat-sen's statue was sculpted by Mr. Jiang Xiaojian, seven months have passed. After several revisions in between, it was not until yesterday that the representatives of the five standing organs of the Municipal Government completed the review. The details are recorded as follows:

Solemn and Grand 71

The model is a standing statue, 8 feet high, and 9 feet high including the base. The whole is white. Wearing a mandarin jacket and long gown, the right hand holds a felt hat hanging down to the knee, and the left hand holds a cane. Energetic, solemn, and grand, making people respectfully admire.

Lifelike 72

Mr. Jiang Xiaojian, who made the model, told the reporter of the Shen Shi News Agency that the model started construction in July or August last year. After several revisions in between, it was finally completed today. The model is based on a photo taken in Tianjin before Sun Yat-sen's death, which is better than the average half-body or full-body, so the shape is lifelike.

Attendees 73

The representatives attending the meeting yesterday were Lin Yannan from the Municipal Government, Bao Sheng from the Garrison Headquarters, Jiang Huaisu from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Wang Xiaolai from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Fan Shuzhi from the Two-Roads Management Bureau, and Shi Weijun from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Those attending the meeting were Shen Yi from the Public Works Bureau.

Resolutions 74

After taking photos in front of the model of Sun Yat-sen's statue, the representatives of each agency continued to hold the ninth standing meeting of the Construction Committee. Chairman Wang Xiaolai presided over the meeting as usual and resolved (1) most of the models are well-made, but the hem of the long gown is too small and the felt hat is too large, and should be corrected appropriately; (2) Director Sun has already seen the model, but the glabella is slightly low and should be raised, the chest is too high and should be lowered, and the cane should also be slightly improved; (3) The cornerstone has been moved to the city center area, and the groundbreaking ceremony will no longer be held. The opening ceremony will be held as originally planned on November 12; (4) The contract will be transferred by the Municipal Government to the Public Works Bureau to sign with the engineer in charge of construction. The construction cost is said to be 12,000 yuan. 5,000 yuan will be paid upon signing the contract, and another 5,000 yuan will be paid after completion. The remaining 2,000 yuan will be paid after the installation is completed and all parties express satisfaction.

City Party Headquarters Telegram to the Central Government 75

Requesting the Appointment of Chiang Kai-shek as Commander-in-Chief

The Guomin News Agency reports: The City Party Headquarters yesterday sent a telegram to the Central Government, addressed to the Nanjing Central Executive Committee: "We respectfully submit that while the committee system of military control is not without its merits, it is suitable for peacetime but not for wartime. Moreover, in modern national warfare, not only military power and command must be centralized and unified, but also the national management of food, financial regulation, and other important industries must all be subordinate to military control. Only by concentrating the power of the entire nation under a centralized command can we achieve comprehensive planning and appropriate responses, thereby achieving the remarkable effect of defeating the enemy and achieving victory. Now, as our country faces a powerful enemy pressing upon our borders and difficulties increasing daily, both resisting the enemy and suppressing bandits are of the utmost importance, concerning the survival of the nation and the life and death of the race. If there is no centralized power and unified command, we will inevitably suffer piecemeal defeat by the enemy. The loss of Eastern Liaoning and the fall of Jehol are still painful reminders, and the lessons of the past are not far off. Now that Chairman Chiang is stationed in North China, directing everything, we respectfully request that your Committee promptly deliberate and resolve to grant him the position of Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, so that he may have complete command and make agile use of it. The future of resisting the Japanese and suppressing bandits truly depends on this." Respectfully submitted by the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipality.

Frontline Battle Report of the Song Army 76

Sun Longji, the representative in Shanghai of the 29th Army Commander Song Zheyuan, received a telegram from Commander Song yesterday reporting on the frontline battle situation. Excerpts from the original telegram are recorded below:

Clever Telegram 77

(Titles omitted) "The enemy is attacking the Luowenyu and Shanzhayu areas. Our officers and soldiers waited for the enemy to approach our positions before wielding their swords and striking directly, resulting in countless corpses. We even captured a cavalry captain alive, while the rest fled in panic. At noon, the enemy, with even larger infantry and artillery units, coordinated their forces and attacked Shanzhayu. The enemy bombarded us with dozens of cannons, raining down shells. The enemy took the opportunity to advance on both sides of our positions. Regiment Commander Li Zenzhi personally supervised his troops, bravely fighting back with extreme ferocity. Regiment Commander Li was unfortunately wounded, yet he continued to direct the battle despite his severe injuries. Our Regiment Commander Qiu Zhiyuan led Wang Hechun's battalion to reinforce us, engaging in five hours of bloody hand-to-hand combat, killing five hundred enemies. Battalion Commander Wang Hechun was killed in action. The enemy infantry and cavalry launched a strong assault on Xifengkou, resulting in hours of fierce fighting. The enemy suffered heavy casualties and was repelled by us." Respectfully submitted by Song Zheyuan, guarding the frontier with skill.

Hao Yi Telegram 78

(Titles omitted) "The enemy facing Luowenyu and Shanzhayukou launched a full-scale attack on our positions last night. Our Division Commander Liu Ruming personally went to the front lines, supervising the Huang unit in a desperate defense. He also dispatched Brigade Commander Li Jintian with a regiment of soldiers to launch a flanking attack on the enemy from the Shabao Yugou Pass. Near Kuaihuo Lin, they were detected by the enemy and came under heavy fire. Our officers and soldiers, disregarding their own safety, drew their swords and charged into the enemy lines, slaughtering countless numbers. At the same time, our Division Commander Liu, seeing the enemy's lines wavering, immediately ordered all units to launch a full-scale attack, attacking from both front and rear. After a night of bloody fighting, we completely cleared the enemy from the areas of Kuaihuoli, Chayukou, Xiaozhengbeiyu, Gushanzi, Shuiquanyu, Madaogou, and Cimeihuayu. Our wounded battalion commanders are Liu Zixiang and Yin Xigan, and other officers and soldiers have suffered heavy casualties. Currently, there are no enemy traces within ten miles north of Luowenyu. (2) According to reliable reports, there are large reinforcements arriving from their rear, seemingly shifting towards our left flank. Division Commander Liu has been instructed to pay special attention and prevent their counterattack. (3) In the Xifengkou area, there were only small-scale conflicts with guerrilla forces last night. This morning, three enemy aircraft dropped over a dozen bombs at Saheqiao and Santunying, wounding several civilians." Specially delivered, Song Zheyuan. Hao Yi.

This is a critical moment. Destroying one's home to relieve the nation's crisis has historical precedent. Jiang Zuobin 86

Discusses Policy Towards Japan

To Visit Wang in Nanjing in Three Days

Ambassador Jiang Zuobin, after completing his official business in the north and returning to Nanjing, took the night express train to Shanghai to rest. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited Jiang at his residence yesterday and was granted an interview. The following points were discussed:

Consistent Policy Towards Japan 87

According to Jiang, "My trip to the north was for reporting purposes. Minister Luo was in North China dealing with certain diplomatic issues, making contact with the embassies of various countries in China and explaining that our country has no choice but to engage in resistance. Rumors of direct negotiations are purely speculative fabrications intended to confuse the public. The people of the country should not believe them. Since Japan has repeatedly engaged in violence and aggression, our government's diplomacy towards Japan has consistently followed its established policy, without any possibility of change. This can be seen in Minister Luo's recent statements, and I might as well reiterate it for the benefit of the people."

Only Way Out is Resistance 88

"Regarding the international situation, the United States, Russia, France, Italy, and other countries have all expressed sympathy towards us in this Sino-Japanese issue. However, their positions and circumstances vary, and due to their own interests, they cannot provide actual assistance. Therefore, the only way out for our country is to struggle arduously and actively resist."

Military Preparations are Complete and Thorough 89

The reporter then asked about the military situation in the north, stating that while our army has repeatedly defeated the enemy and achieved victories, it is unknown if there are any other supply preparations besides the front lines. Jiang replied that in addition to the complete and thorough arrangements in the front-line positions, Chairman Chiang has made ample preparations for subsequent supplies. Moreover, all military commanders throughout the country are determined to resist Japan. Therefore, they will do their utmost to resist and defend against the enemy.

Will Meet With Wang Again Within Days 90

"I (Jiang referring to himself) originally planned to report everything to President Wang in Nanjing, but after hearing that President Wang was staying in Shanghai for a few more days, I rushed to Shanghai. However, our paths did not cross. Since returning to the country, I have been constantly traveling and have not had any rest. The journey has been tiring, and I feel quite exhausted. Therefore, I have decided to rest in Shanghai for a few days and then go to Nanjing in three days to meet with President Wang. As for when I will return to my post, I am still unable to decide."

Dependents Arriving Today or Tomorrow

133 Women and Children, Mrs. Wang Accompanying, Representatives Contacting Various Organizations to Arrange Accommodations. Zhang stated that he, along with Li Du's representative Liu Piguang and Ma Zhanshan's representative Wu Huanzhang, contacted the Shanghai Municipal Government and various organizations such as the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association and the Northeast Refugee Relief Association to arrange accommodations. The reporter also inquired with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and a person in charge stated that the Wu Yang had already arrived in Yantai and was heading south. They had received a telegram, but it was unknown whether it would stop in Qingdao. However, it is estimated that it will arrive in Shanghai today or tomorrow at the latest. Zhang Chuyu's letter to the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association requesting assistance reads as follows: "Respectfully, due to the fact that the dependents of our army's Commander-in-Chief Wang and other generals are returning to the country from Vladivostok and departed from Tanggu on the 17th, taking a ship to Shanghai, they are expected to arrive soon. I am instructed by Representative Liang Detang to inform the Liaoning-Jilin Support Association and the Jilin Headquarters, requesting that they inform various organizations to arrange for care. A copy of the original telegram is enclosed for your perusal. I pray for your attention to this matter." Sincerely, the Shanghai Liaison Office of the National Salvation Army Commander-in-Chief Wang Delin. March 20th.

Second Batch 93

Antiquities Arriving Today

Totaling 1,564 Boxes

The Guowen News Agency reports: The first batch of 1,054 boxes of antiquities from the Peiping Palace Museum have been transported to Shanghai and stored at the former Renji Hospital at No. 26 Tianzhutang Street. The authorities of the Chinese Settlement and Song Ziwen, acting as the head of the Executive Yuan, have sent personnel to provide strict protection. The museum's Secretary-General Li Zongtong and Secretary Wu Ying have returned to the north. The second batch of antiquities has also left Peiping and arrived in Nanjing and will also be transported to Shanghai for storage. The second batch consists of 1,564 boxes, which is more than the previous batch. However, 70 of these boxes contain antiquities from the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica, mostly bronzes, jades, and paintings. Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received a telegram from Nanjing stating that the Kuailli (Fast Profit) ship carrying the antiquities had set sail for Shanghai in the afternoon. Therefore, it is expected that this batch of antiquities will arrive at the pier by ship this afternoon, berthing at the Jinliyuan Wharf on Xinkai River. Yesterday afternoon, the reporter returned to the storage location to inquire. It was stated that the second batch of antiquities is expected to arrive at the warehouse this afternoon or tomorrow morning. Councilor Chen of the Executive Yuan is responsible for their safekeeping. Yu Tongkui, who escorted the second batch south, is expected to arrive on the same ship tomorrow. When the second batch left Peiping, it was escorted by 150 military police officers sent from Peiping to Nanjing. It is believed that after arriving in Nanjing, they will be transferred to the Capital Military Police for escort to Shanghai. After arriving in Shanghai, Maotai Transportation Company trucks will still be hired, and under the protection of military police, the goods will be unloaded and transported to the warehouse.

Another report states that the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica has shipped more than 30 books with the second batch of antiquities from Peiping. After arriving in Nanjing, they were transferred to a freight train on the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway and arrived in Shanghai yesterday for preservation.

Our business community should not be involved in this kind of malady, which would lead to the failure of everything due to too much discussion and too little success. Novel Fundraising Method 101

Chuan Hongtao, residing at No. 473 Julai Road in the French Concession, has recently created a new method for fundraising for aircraft. It essentially involves each citizen of the Republic of China donating one copper coin per day, each coin being equivalent to 0.003333 silver yuan. With a population of over 460 trillion people nationwide (excluding the three northeastern provinces), the daily donation of copper coins would amount to over 1.56 million silver yuan. Monthly, this would raise over 47 million yuan, and annually, over 560 million yuan. Considering the price of each aircraft to be 150,000 silver yuan, over 3,733 aircraft could be purchased in a year. The procedure is simple and the effect is significant. However, how to collect and centralize these donations poses a problem. It is said that Mr. Chuan has devised a proper method for this. Those who wish to know the details can contact Mr. Chuan directly.
