Page 9

Japanese Troops Pour into Rehe 109

The Opportunity to Recover the Northeast Has Arrived

Puppet Troops Plan to Revolt,　　Underground Resistance Begins to Mobilize　　Deng Wen and Li Haiqing in Dolun

Deng Wen, formerly of the Heilongjiang Volunteer Army Command and representative of Li Mingxin of the 2nd Army of Ma Zhanshan, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday from the north to contact various organizations and provide aid to the volunteer army to recover the three northeastern provinces. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited him at his residence yesterday morning to discuss the situation of the troops retreating from Rehe and Heilongjiang and the current state of the Northeast. The details are as follows:

Deng and Li Retreat to Chahar 110

Deng Wen and Li Haiqing's troops, totaling over 20,000 men, retreated to Rehe Province due to a lack of ammunition and supplies in Heilongjiang. They first stationed in Kailu, where they received 100,000 rounds of ammunition and 200 rounds of artillery shells from the Beiping Military Branch and the Liaojihei Support Association, which was insufficient for distribution. The Military Branch promised to replenish anti-aircraft guns, machine guns, and ammunition, but they had not arrived by the time the war began and they were forced to retreat to Linxi. Later, affected by the loss of Chengde, they retreated to Dolun. Exhausted from prolonged fighting and lacking food and supplies, they hoped to receive sufficient replenishment and support so that they could continue to fight the enemy.

The Three Eastern Provinces are Empty 111

The Japanese troops currently being transferred to attack Rehe are the same troops that were stationed in the three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang. The main force has already been sent to Rehe, so the Japanese military strength in the three provinces is very weak. Both Heilongjiang and Jilin provinces only have three to five hundred men stationed in the provincial capitals and trading ports. The rest of the defenses are handled by the puppet troops. However, the puppet troops have not forgotten their homeland and have suffered bullying from the Japanese, harboring resentment. They are temporarily enduring and submitting to preserve their strength and await an opportunity to act because the central government has no concrete action to recover the lost territories. Now that the central armies have officially planned to fight the brutal Japanese, the puppet troops all plan to revolt.

A Rare Opportunity 112

In August of last year, the Heilongjiang armies received a handwritten letter from Zhang Hanqing, stating that failing to avenge national and personal grievances would make them unworthy of being human. He decided to lead his 20 brigades out of the pass to recover the lost territories. Wang Zhizhe's six brigades went first, opening the gateway to the Northeast. Su Bingwen, 㯷 Bingshan, and others were encouraged by the news and rose up to fight the enemy. As a result, the Japanese army launched an all-out invasion to the north and defeated them one by one because the interior of the country was unable to send troops. Su and Ma retreated to Russian territory, and Deng Wen, Li Haiqing, and others led their troops to Rehe. However, 㯷's troops remained in Heilongjiang Province, lurking in the deep mountains, with a strength of about 20,000 men. But they face difficulties in supplies, and their clothing and shoes are incomplete. Recently, they have begun to mobilize towards the cities. There are many other underground resistance forces. If they receive sufficient support and rise up together, taking advantage of the fact that the Japanese are focusing all their efforts on fighting in Rehe and the three eastern provinces are empty, and if the armies within the pass launch an attack again, it will not be difficult to recover the lost territories in one fell swoop, allowing the people of Liaodong to see the clothing and culture of Han Chinese again.

Zhang Youqun Went to Beijing Last Night 113

Japanese Troops in Northern Rehe Transferred to Reinforce; Intense Fighting Expected Soon

Sun Dianying, the commander of the 41st Army, sent his representative Zhang Youqun to Shanghai to report to all sectors on the army's arduous fighting in northern Rehe and to seek assistance. It is learned that Representative Zhang has completed his mission in Shanghai and will take the overnight express train to Beijing last night to make contact with the Military Council. According to Representative Zhang, he received a telegram from the Chief of Staff Feng of our army this morning (the 20th) stating that the enemy has been transferring large numbers of fresh troops for reinforcement in recent days, and that intense fighting is expected to occur within the next day or two. He hopes that all parties will provide material assistance to enable him to fight to the end. He will enter Beijing tonight, and whether he will return north or come to Shanghai again will be decided after consulting with Commander Sun.

Instructions from the Ministry of Industry 114

Participate in the International Trade Conference

The purpose is to jointly adopt a free economic policy. The Ministry of Industry yesterday instructed He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, stating that it had received a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding a letter and regulations from the Chinese Embassy in France, which had forwarded a letter from the International Export Trade Association inviting Chinese businesses to join the International Trade Conference to be held in Paris in April of this year. The relevant letter and regulations are attached for your review and action. In addition to replying, you are instructed to forward the attached documents to the China International Trade Association, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and all relevant organizations for their information. The original letter stated, "To Whom It May Concern: We have recently received a letter from the International Export Trade Association stating that Mr. Gaulow, a representative of the association, contacted your embassy regarding the International Trade Conference to be held at the International Chamber of Commerce in Paris from April 24 to 30. The purpose of the organization is to enable producers and exporters from all countries to establish contact, jointly adopt a free economic policy, and form an International Export Industry Committee, which, in conjunction with the International Chamber of Commerce, will work to restore international trade to its original state as soon as possible. Many businesses in the export industry in Europe and the Americas have joined the association. If your country's export industry or chamber of commerce can send representatives to attend, the association would be extremely welcome. Please forward this letter to your government and inform all relevant parties." (The following is omitted).

Philippines 115

Will Send Personnel to China to Investigate Industries

Preparing a Complete Plan for Independence from the United States, This Important Matter Instructs Preparation for Hospitality

The Ministry of Industry yesterday instructed the International Trade Bureau of this city, stating that it had received a report from the Consul General in Manila stating that the Philippine authorities have been working hard to achieve independence from the United States. The U.S. government is deeply understanding of this request, and although the implementation methods have not been decided, it is likely to become a reality in the near future. Since the Philippines came under the control of the United States, trade between the two countries has been free according to regulations.

Philippine Goods Transported to America 116

Statistics in recent years show that they account for about 80% of total exports. The Philippines is an agricultural country, and its main products include sugar, hemp, rice, coconut, tobacco, and timber. Now, it is facing overproduction, sluggish overseas sales, and falling prices. Therefore, developing local products and overseas markets is both essential to addressing the issue of independence and an urgent task. The Philippine government has already begun to make concrete plans for this.

With Regards to Our Country 117

It is paying particular attention. At the end of last year, Philippine Governor Roosevelt sent his counselor, Colonel Cary I. Crockett, to China for investigation in preparation. The council recently decided to send four members to form a delegation to investigate in various parts of our country in preparation for a complete plan. It can be seen that Mr. Crockett's trip last year left a very good impression. The four members are (Marcelo T. Boncan Jnan L. Luna Jose E. Romero Jose A. Ozamis). In addition, there are four specialized committee members (Prof. Vientr G. Sinco Prof. Jose A. Espiritn Rep. Gregorio Nieva Atty. Quintin Paredes Jr.). Before this plan was finalized, member (MaeCrceLo T. Boncan) informally contacted the consulate regarding the Philippines' desire to develop commerce in other countries. As the Consul General, I believe that China and the Philippines are close neighbors,

Chinese Immigrants in the Philippines 118

Number in the tens of thousands, requiring considerable support. In recent years, the authorities have been devising unfavorable measures against foreign merchants and imported goods in order to increase tax revenue and protect local products. One example of this is the increase in import tariffs on eggs and other items implemented last year. The Philippines has a trade surplus with the United States, and its foreign trade, other than with the United States, is mostly imports. Therefore, there is little fear of retaliation from other countries. If the Philippines' commerce with our country improves in the future, these restrictions will naturally be lifted. Therefore, I expressed deep sympathy for the member's contact. At that time, I indicated that we should find a way to eliminate the parts of the tariff increase last year that were biased against Chinese goods in order to show mutual benefit. The member also indicated that there was room for discussion. The delegation is currently preparing everything and tentatively plans to depart on the President Taft on March 29. All of the reasons for the Philippine delegation's

Investigation in China 119

Concerning Commerce, are included in this formal report to the department for your review. Furthermore, the members of the delegation are all high-ranking officials in the Philippines, and their mission is extremely important. It seems necessary to provide them with hospitality and facilities for their investigation. This is attached for your consideration and processing.

Customs to Use 120

Newly Minted Silver Dollars for Fee Collection Starting Yesterday

The Jianghai Customs Commissioner issued a notice yesterday morning stating that (1) passenger permits for incoming and outgoing travelers, (2) inland port fees, (3) permits for Chinese merchant ships carrying foreign crew members, (4) permits for ships from countries without consulates carrying Chinese crew members, (5) consular service fees, (6) permits for loading and unloading goods outside the port, (7) fees for copying customs documents or paying taxes, (8) fees for oil storage, (9) fees for assembling automobile storage licenses, and (10) regular surveillance fees for customs officials, etc., will all be collected in newly minted silver standard currency starting today (i.e., yesterday).

Fisheries Improvement Association of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces 121

Establishment of a Fisheries Construction Fee Collection Office

The temporary meeting yesterday approved Dai Yongtang and others as directors; collection will begin on April 15 with a tax rate of 1% of value

The Fisheries Improvement Association of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces convened a temporary meeting at 3:00 p.m. yesterday to discuss the collection of fisheries construction fees. The attendees included Chen Gongbo (represented by Liu Xingji), Wu Xingya (represented by Wu Chengru), Dong Xiujia (represented by Wang Wentai), Du Yuesheng (represented by Hu Hu), Lin Genghou, Wu Zhenpan, Chen Zhongsheng, Dai Yongtang, Zhou Jianyin, Hou Zhaohai, Zhang Shenzhi (represented by Dong Xincen), Fang Jiaobo (represented by Chen Qibo), and Zeng Yangfu (represented by He Huiyu). The meeting was chaired by Chen Gongbo (represented by Liu Xingji). The items discussed included: (1) Commissioner Fang Jiaobo's proposal that the collection of fisheries construction fees should be handled by a specialized office established by the association, which was approved. (2) Commissioner Du Yuezhong's proposal that the initial rate for the collection of fisheries construction fees should be temporarily set at 1% of value to facilitate implementation, which was approved. (3) The joint proposal from the Economic Group and the Standing Committee that the proposed rules had already been submitted to the Ministry for approval by the association, which was approved retroactively. (4) The organizational charter for the Construction Fee Collection Office, which was approved with amendments. (5) The rules for penalties for the Collection Office, which were approved with amendments. (6) Commissioner Lin Kanghou's proposal to draft service rules for the revenue officers, which was approved and assigned to the Collection Office to draft and submit to the association for approval and implementation. (7) The rules for the custody and payment of construction fees, which were approved and referred to the Custody Group for reference. (8) The rules for auditing construction fees, which were approved and referred to the Audit Group for reference. (9) The proposal by Director Chen of the Economic Group to appoint Commissioner Dai Yongtang as the director of the association's Construction Fee Collection Office, which was approved. (10) Commissioner Zhou Jianyin's proposal to set April 15 as the date for the commencement of construction fee collection, which was approved. (11) Commissioner Lin Kanghou's proposal that the portion of the fisheries construction fees collected from freshwater products should be used exclusively for the construction of inland river fisheries, which was approved with the principle that the allocation of fisheries construction fees should simultaneously focus on the organization and construction of inland river fisheries, and the Design Group was requested to draft a plan for the organization and construction of inland river fisheries in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. (12) Commissioner Dong Xiujia's proposal that the fisheries and aquatic education institutions in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces should be exempt from the fisheries construction fee, which was rejected and it was decided that the fees should still be collected, stored separately, and used as subsidies for the fisheries experiments and aquatic education institutions in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

Road Bureau Moves to New Location for Office Yesterday 123

Traffic Department Relocation Still Under Consideration

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, formerly located at the small and cramped Bazilu (靶子路) address, found it inadequate for office space and inconvenient as its various departments were not centrally located. Consequently, a new location was sought, and the second floor of the Riverside Mansion at the intersection of North Suzhou Road and Henan Road was rented as the new headquarters. Last Saturday and Sunday, during the holiday, the administration first moved the General Affairs, Engineering, and Mechanical Departments. Yesterday, Monday, operations commenced at the new location. The Materials and Accounting Departments, however, could not move until the renovations of the new premises are completed, which is expected to be by this Sunday. The old Bazilu headquarters, now vacant, has already been hired for repairs and will be used to relocate the Medical Department as a railway hospital. As for the Traffic Department, due to a temporary suspension of the Northern Station's relocation order, the plan is to slightly renovate the burned-out building for the department's office use, but this is currently still under consideration and no decision has been made.

Great Central Factory Accepts Workers' Demands; Mediation Successful, Both Parties Very Satisfied

The unemployed workers of the Taishan Rubber Factory had previously heard that the factory was being sold to Chinese owners and renamed the Great Central Factory. Second Municipal Federation, Fourth Branch Discusses an Important Case 130

The Fourth District Branch of the Shanghai Second Special District Citizen Federation held its sixth executive committee meeting yesterday at 8:00 PM. Eleven committee members were present, with Xu Xiuting presiding. After the report, the following issues were discussed: (1) The French Concession Water and Electricity Company has already implemented the recent increase in tram fares. According to reports, the company's business situation, due to its monopoly, is exceptionally developed, with an average annual profit of over one million yuan after expenses. Now, this thriving and highly profitable company has suddenly increased prices, disregarding the burden on the city. It is also rumored that water rates will also be increased. This association should express its opposition. Resolution: (A) Based on the company's business situation, send a letter to the Chinese directors of the French Concession Taxpayers' Association to conduct detailed research and express opposition. (B) Send a letter to the Municipal Federation and all district branches to unanimously advocate opposition. (2) Abolish Taels and Change to Yuan. The French Concession's municipal donations and water and electricity fees are still calculated in taels, which causes many abuses. The fees should be converted to yuan. Resolution: (A) Send a letter to the Municipal Federation to forward to the Public Works Department to implement reforms immediately. (B) Send separate letters to the French Concession Taxpayers' Association and the district branches of the Municipal Federation to unanimously urge the realization of this goal. (C) Notify citizens to comply uniformly. (3) Discuss several cases of members being fined by the police for freight trucks. Adjourned.

Nanyang Company 131

Worker Slowdown Causes Disturbance

Conflict Erupts, Two Employees Injured; Party and Government Persuade, Work Resumes in the Afternoon; Company to Respond to Six Conditions Tomorrow Morning

According to Dagon News Agency, Nanyang Tobacco Company at the intersection of East Broadway Road and Zhaofeng Road was once closed in 1929 due to declining business and capital losses. Subsequently, all employees voluntarily reduced their wages and cooperated sincerely with the factory, so the business has gradually improved in recent years. Recently, over 2,700 male and female workers in the factory, in order to unite consistently, presented to the Municipal Party Department and organized the Nanyang Office of the Fourth District Cigarette Workers' Union, which was formally established on the 12th of this month. On the 16th, they submitted six preliminary conditions to the factory: (1) The Company recognizes the Shanghai Fourth District Cigarette Industry Union and the Nanyang Cigarette Factory Office as having the right to represent all factory workers; (2) No factory employees may be dismissed without reason; (3) Wage increases, a monthly bonus of three yuan, and the bonus work money of 96 days per person for 1932, calculated as an average of eight days per month for twelve months, should be combined and included in wages; (4) The Company shall subsidize the Nanyang Cigarette Factory Office with 500 yuan per month to carry out employee benefit activities; (5) Female cigarette packers and cigarette workers for soft and hard packs must have their wages increased by two cents per 1,000 cigarettes, large packs must have their wages increased by two li per ten packs, canned goods must have their wages increased by one cent per twenty cans, and box gluing must have their wages increased by two cents per 100 boxes; (6) These preliminary conditions for labor and management shall apply until the official conditions for labor and management are signed. However, no response was received. Yesterday morning, all workers automatically started to slow down work. The officials of the union office then sent representatives, Wu Shiyuan, to report to the Municipal Party Department, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the General Labor Union, requesting mediation. Another group of officials, Zhang Desheng, etc., went to the company's office to discuss solutions with the factory. At that time, the office staff, seeing the large number of workers, feared disturbances and closed the gate, refusing entry. This led to a conflict. As a result, Li Zitang, director of the cigarette packing department, and Li Zihui, director of the tobacco drying room, were injured in the assault, and the order was quite chaotic. When the Huishan Police Station received the report, they immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to the scene to suppress it. The injured were taken to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, and a representative of the transportation machinery, Zhang Decheng, was taken into custody by the police station. After receiving the report from the labor side, party and government agencies sent Zhang Sheng, director of the People's Movement Section of the Municipal Party Department, and Wang Xianqing, director of the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, along with Zhu Xuefan and Bai Shaoxu, members of the General Labor Union, and Zhou Xuexiang, representative of the Fourth District Cigarette Workers' Union, to the company's general office at 10:00 AM yesterday to mediate. Assistant Manager Jian Yingfu and legal advisor Wu Linkun received them and called on representatives from the labor side to discuss solutions. After further consultation, the following was decided: (1) The company stated that, in principle, it accepted the six conditions proposed by the labor side and agreed to conduct formal negotiations within one or two days; (2) The company was responsible for finding a way to bail out the detained worker representative; (3) Party, government, and labor union representatives were responsible for persuading the workers who were slowing down to resume work first and wait for a legal solution. It was also decided that at 4:00 PM, negotiations would continue at the company. After the party and government representatives consulted and made a decision, the representatives went to the factory's rooftop platform to summon all the male and female workers, report the results of the consultation, and Wang Xianqing of the Social Affairs Bureau, Zhu Xuefan of the General Labor Union, and Wu Shiyuan, the representative of the labor side, all persuaded the workers in turn. Wu Linkun, the company's representative, also replied. The workers followed the advice of the superiors and resumed work at 2:30 PM, working as usual. The party and government representatives went to the company again at 4:00 PM to continue discussions with the company representative Wu Linkun. Regarding the conditions proposed by the labor side, Mr. Wu stated that the company had already handed over the conditions to labor consultant Zhu Maocheng for detailed study and consideration, so he could not express a definitive statement at the time. An official response would be given on the 22nd (tomorrow) morning. As for the detained worker Zhang Decheng, the police station did not agree to release him, but the company would still find a way to secure his bail.

Inhumanity 133

Slaughtering One's Own Newborn Child

Two children born consecutively died young and infertile.

The Ningbo region has a barbaric custom of killing newborn babies.

It is said that future births will then be ensured of survival.

Chen Along actually resorted to such a heinous act.

Last Saturday night at 9:30 PM, two Chinese detectives, No. 2017 and No. 3041 from the Xinzha Police Station, were patrolling near the Xinzha Road bridgehead. They saw a man, appearing to be in his late twenties, hurrying towards the Suzhou River carrying a bamboo basket. The basket was covered with a large tattered cloth. Suspecting something amiss, the detectives ordered him to stop. Upon removing the cloth for inspection, they discovered a naked infant, covered in blood, inside the basket, who had clearly been stabbed to death. The detectives immediately took the man and the basket containing the corpse back to the police station to report the incident. The police chief then dispatched Detective Tao Rubing to investigate. It was revealed that the man carrying the basket was named Wang Jinyan, a native of Shaoxing, residing at No. 2 Xinzha Road. The baby was born to the wife of Chen Along, a Ningbo native who works as a laborer at the water company and resides at No. 465 Xinzha Road, only five days prior, and had been personally murdered by Chen. Chen Along was 36 years old and had no children. He had been married for nine years. His first son lived to the age of six before succumbing to illness. Later, a daughter was born, but she also died young at the age of only three. Chen's elderly mother, distressed by this, told him of a barbaric custom in Ningbo. She said that if a child is born and does not thrive, the newborn should be killed to ensure future children are healthy. Chen believed this. This time, his wife became pregnant, and on the 13th of this month, she gave birth for the third time. The baby was a boy and cried loudly. The whole family was overjoyed. Unexpectedly, three days later, the baby suddenly fell ill and grew increasingly weaker. By the night of the 18th, he was barely breathing and beyond saving. Chen recalled his mother's words and believed that if he did not sacrifice this child, he would never have healthy children. A murderous intent arose within him. He grabbed a sharp kitchen knife and waited in a secluded alley outside the back door of his house. He asked his friend, Wang Jinyan, to bring the sick baby out of the house. Chen cruelly raised the knife and slashed at the baby's head. With one blow, blood splattered everywhere, and the baby's life was extinguished. This inhuman act, born of superstition, is utterly cruel. Chen then found a bamboo basket, placed the baby's corpse inside, covered it with a bed sheet to conceal it, and asked Wang to carry it to the Suzhou River to throw it into the murky water and let it be food for the fish. Unexpectedly, they were discovered by the patrolmen. The baby's body was sent to the forensic examination office on Avenue Petain. Yesterday morning, a report was submitted to the First Special District Court, and Prosecutor Guo Wei was commissioned to examine the body. The examination confirmed that the baby had died from a head wound. The corpse was handed over to the Pushan Public Cemetery for burial. The two suspects, Chen Along and Wang Jinyan, were brought to the First Special District Court this morning. Judge Qian Wenji conducted a preliminary hearing. First, the police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, explained the circumstances of the case, stating that the defendants' actions constituted the crime of murder under Article 282 of the Criminal Law and should be prosecuted accordingly. Judge Qian then briefly questioned the two defendants and ordered them to be remanded in custody for further interrogation at a later date.

(1) Wu Zhongxing's "Lingering Sun on the Whip," (2) Jiang Jinzhi's "Dawn of the East," (3) Shen Yan's "Grapes," (4) Huang Qianzhang's "Oil Paint," (5) Zhai Peiqing's "Holy Night," (6) Ye Qianyu's "Carriage," (7) Liu Xucang's "Dawn," Fourteen people were awarded prizes of excellence, including (1) Jin Shisheng's "Chrysanthemum," (2) Chu Zuyin's "Reeds Under the Mountain," (3) Shen Yan's "Shepherd," (4) Flying Peng Art Society's "Basket," (5) Wang Yuhuai's "Pearl on a Plate," (6) Wu Zhongxing's "Qiong Lin," (7) Wu Zhongxing's "Taihu Lake," (8) Wu Zhongxing's "Deafening," (9) Liu Xucang's "Birds," (10) Liu Xucang's "Peacock," (11) Xia Kesheng's "Fisherman's Harvest," (12) Gan Naiguang's "Wooden Bucket," (13) Time Press's "Shadow," (14) Cai Renbao's "Spring River Warms," For the landscape and historical site category, the three receiving first prize were (1) Chu Minyi's "Immortal's Palm on Mount Hua, Shaanxi," (2) Zhang Daqian's "Huangshan, Anhui," (3) Ji Guanghua's "Tianmu Mountain Waterfall, Zhejiang," The eight who were awarded prizes of excellence were (1) Lu Yucang's "Taihao Main Hall," (2) Huang Zhongchang's "On the Road to Moganshan, Zhejiang," (3) Xu Tonglai's "Jingbo Lake Waterfall," (4) Li Wenji's "Wanxian Lu'an Bridge," (5) Lin Jingzhi's "Lanzhou Leitanshui Reclining Bridge, Gansu," (6) Shu Xincheng's "A Panoramic View of the River and Sky," (7) ORLY's "Qiantang River, Hangzhou," (8) Yang Peng's "Yun Ti in Hengshan, Hunan" After the evaluation, the committee held a meeting to discuss the award method. Those who wish to purchase photos should go immediately, lest they regret it. The Municipal Government Approves Exemption of Wusong Handcart Tax 134

A Six-Month Grace Period Starting from April

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously submitted a request from the Wusong Branch Office, asking the Municipal Government to exempt the human-powered cart tax. The original request was forwarded and approved for exemption, as previously reported in various newspapers. It is now known that the Municipal Government has officially replied to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce with the approval for the tax exemption. The original reply stated, "The request is noted. Based on the report, the carts in the area have special circumstances. A temporary exemption for the cart tax is granted, effective from April of this year for six months. Taxes owed previously should be paid according to regulations. During the exemption period, all unregistered carts must still be reported to the Wusong Vehicle Affairs Office of the Public Utilities Bureau for registration. Registered carts must still obtain lead tax permits from the Wusong Cart Tax Office of the Finance Bureau on a monthly basis, with a permit fee of 5 cents per cart to show consideration. In addition to ordering the Public Utilities and Finance Bureaus to comply, you are to immediately notify them of this approval."

Criminals Wu Jigui and Others Escorted to Suzhou

The criminals Wu Jigui, Zhang Changlin, Zhang Shaoliang, Song Jiande, and others who assassinated Wu Guangzong, the director of the Naval Survey Bureau, committed the crime in the concession area and were apprehended by the police. Jianye Lane 136

The Origin of the Discovery of a Minor Kidnapping Case

Jiang Adong, the six-year-old son of Jiang Desheng, who lived in Jianye Lane, Rue Foch, in the French Concession, was kidnapped on February 13th for ransom. The French Police Special Operations Unit detectives apprehended six suspects including the kidnapper Zhou Liansheng and rescued the victim. The criminals were handed over to the Second Special District Court for trial. There were omissions in previous reports, and this is a special supplement. According to the victims, eight ransom letters were received from the kidnappers, signed by Wang Jinzhang and bearing a seal. The important phrases in the letters were also sealed. The letters referred to the "Commander-in-Chief of the Northeast Volunteer United Army" or "Commander of this Army," claiming that the military situation in the Northeast was urgent, and the soldiers were in dire need of funds. The letters demanded 15,000 yuan for military expenses, promising to repay the principal and interest after the matter was completed. They instructed the victim not to report to the police, threatening to kill the entire family if the police were involved. In the third letter, there was a pair of cut red papers, with the character "Fu" written on top and the word "contract" spelled out below. The left half of the small square was to be used by the victim as a token of representation. When contacting the bandits, it was used for verification. They also instructed the representative to hold a knife of grass paper and two bottles of medicinal wine as a sign. In one letter, the kidnappers did not affix stamps and instead used two 2-cent revenue stamps, causing the victim to be fined by the post office for insufficient postage. After receiving the letters, the victim sent his neighbor Chen Abing as a representative to negotiate at the front doors of the Old Oriental Hotel and the Wu Palace Hotel, and along the section of Xizang Road from the Far East Hotel north to Yikouxiang. However, the bandits' exorbitant demands led to no result. The final meeting was arranged at the Huayang Hotel, but the secret was leaked, and the French police learned of it, leading to the arrest of the kidnappers. The victim has now submitted the eight letters to the police for submission to the court as evidence. In the meantime, the police have ordered all detectives to strictly apprehend the fleeing leaders of the gang and bring them to justice for trial.

Recent Financial History of Shanghai 137

Third Edition Published

Mr. Xu Jiqing of Yongjia compiled the book "Recent Financial History of Shanghai" in 1926. A revised and expanded second edition was published in 1929, and it was widely sold both at home and abroad. Because the financial situation in Shanghai has undergone significant changes in recent years due to the changes in the current situation, the author has revised it again, keeping the style the same. The content has been increased by more than double. The content is roughly as follows: (1) The organizational situation and business overview of Chinese and foreign banks, trust companies, and savings associations, with the balance sheets for the past five years attached, (2) The number of shareholders, capital, and number of shares of various money houses in the past five years, (3) The issuance status of national government bonds and treasury bills, (4) The liquidation and closure of various banks and money houses, (5) The organization of the Shanghai Silver and Money Industry Association Joint Preparation Committee and the Clearing House, (6) The problem of abolishing taels and changing to yuan, (7) The completion of the China Credit Investigation Office and the Coinage Factory, etc. Looking at the entire book, the style is rigorous, the collection of materials is extensive and rich, and it can detail the whole process and study the rise and fall. Not only should the financial and industrial sectors have a copy, but it is also an indispensable reference material for academic research. The entire book is divided into two volumes, with a total of more than 1,100 pages and more than 500,000 words. The price is three yuan. Sales locations: Dadong Bookstore on Fourth Malu, Shanghai, Author's Bookstore, Liming Bookstore, Banking Weekly on Hong Kong Road.

Xia Jintang 138

Hosts Guangfu Eye Hospital

Provides Free Diagnosis and Medicine to the Poor and Sick

Dr. Xia Jintang, an ophthalmologist who studied in Japan, originally collaborated with Shibata Hospital. After the September 18th Incident, he broke away. When the January 28th Shanghai Incident broke out, he spied on the enemy's military situation on behalf of our military headquarters. After the incident, the Japanese army raided his home, and his telegrams and codebooks were searched. Xia himself and his entire family were arrested and taken to the Japanese army headquarters. His entire family was released by Japanese neighbors, but Xia himself was still detained at the Japanese army headquarters in the Japanese primary school. He twice narrowly escaped being shot and witnessed Xiang Songmao being shot by the Japanese army on the morning of February 4th at 3 or 4 AM. According to what Dr. Xia personally learned during his detention, no less than one or two thousand Chinese were shot in the Japanese primary school. Subsequently, our Navy Department negotiated with the Japanese side, and Xia was able to regain his freedom after nine deaths and one life. He is now independently operating Guangfu Eye Hospital at No. 5, Lane 63, east of the racecourse. The name Guangfu means resisting Japan. Dr. Xia is an expert in ophthalmology with excellent medical skills. Now, after his painful experience, he runs a hospital and provides free diagnosis and medicine to the poor and sick to help the Chinese people.

Arrest of the Culprit in the Murder of the Watchman 139

Wang Amai, a watchman from Ningbo, 44, at the Wang Maoshun Construction Factory on Hart Road, had been working there for a long time. On January 7th of this year, at 9:15 PM, four thugs, each carrying weapons and lime, broke into the factory. They first tore down the bamboo fence and went straight into Wang's bedroom. They threw lime in Wang's face, then used iron rods and axes to hack at him. Wang, blinded, could not resist and was seriously injured. The attackers fled when they saw their purpose was achieved. Wang's colleague Feng Afu heard the alarm and rushed over, but the attackers were gone. Wang Amai was lying on the bed covered in blood. He reported to the accounting office, who reported to the Xinzha Police Station, ordering detectives to go. Wang was taken to Shilong Hospital but died of his injuries at 12:30 AM. The prosecutor of the First Special District Court examined the body and ordered the police to arrest the perpetrators. Since the case occurred, the police sent Detective Zhao Fuhai Yang Peizhang to investigate, and they finally discovered the cause of the matter. There was a scoundrel from Tianjin named Liu Yuan, nicknamed Tianjin Lao Liu, who was previously a police officer in the Public Security Bureau. Since being dismissed the year before, he had been idle and specialized in forming gangs, stealing wood from construction sites in the western part of Shanghai. In December of last year, Liu was caught stealing wood from Wang Maoshun's factory by Wang Amai, who beat him up and released him. Liu held a grudge and repeatedly thought of revenge. On January 4th, he gathered his gang to discuss and decided to first blind Wang with lime, then use weapons to kill him. On the evening of the 7th, Wang was indeed killed. But Liu had an addiction to opium. Detectives Zhao et al. focused on this and secretly investigated in various opium dens in western Shanghai. Until yesterday, they arrested a suspect named Yue Jiancai from Anhui on Rubenson Road and brought him to the police station. According to Yue, the matter was initiated by Tianjin Lao Liu, who told Yue, Henan Lao Liu, Xiaomanzi, and others to do it together. They then arrested Liu Yuan (Tianjin Lao Liu) and Liu Zhifa separately on the same road. This morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang detailed the above situation, saying that the police are prosecuting Yue Jiancai and Liu Yuan for premeditated murder under Article 284 of the Criminal Law. However, the investigation procedures for Liu Zhifa have not been completed, so he is requested to be detained, and the case should be postponed. Then, witness Feng Afu testified that he was a watchman at Wang Maoshun Construction Factory and a colleague of the deceased. On the evening of January 7th, he suddenly heard Wang's cries for help in his room. He rushed to investigate. It was night, and Wang's room was dark. He brought fire and saw Wang covered in blood, saying that he had been attacked by thugs. He was shocked and reported to the accounting office, who sent Wang to the hospital, but he died shortly after. He did not see the perpetrators. Witnesses Zhou Xiande and Liu Xiqing also testified. When questioned, the defendant Yue Jiancai confessed that Tianjin Lao Liu, Henan Lao Liu, and Xiaomanzi, who is still at large, went with him, and he carried an iron rod. When questioned, Tianjin Lao Liu confessed that he used to be a police officer and was dismissed in May of the year before. He then lived as a peddler and smoked opium, and sometimes stole hats to sell for addiction. However, he vehemently denied the murder of Wang Amai. Liu Zhifa is Henan Lao Liu. Judge Qian Wenji verified the confession and ordered the three defendants to be detained for seven days for further investigation.

Smuggling Case Cracked on Zhoushan Maru Ship 140

Smuggler Remanded to Await Sentencing 141

Detective Wang Guangqi and Hu Guangrong of the Hongkou Police Station apprehended smuggler Lin Pengju, a native of Fujian, and a woman, Lin Yuying (his sister), on the Zhoushan Maru ship at the Wayside Wharf. They seized two children, one five years old and one two years old, and brought them to the police station. They were sent to the First Special District Court. According to the suspects, they spent 200 yuan to buy the two children from poor families in Chongming and Qidong counties through a certain Jia, who is at large, to take them back to their hometown as sons. However, the contract was lost in a hurry. Police investigation revealed that the siblings planned to take the two children to Fujian to sell them to wealthy, childless individuals, and then use the remaining money to buy more children and split the profits with Jia. They were ordered to be remanded in custody for further investigation. The two children were sent to the Women and Children's Relief Association for care. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan and Chief Prosecutor Wang Zuze of the Criminal Court Three continued the trial. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that during the postponement, the police sent letters to the Chongming and Qidong County Courts to investigate whether poor families sold their children and whether any children were kidnapped within their jurisdiction. They have already received a reply, stating that no such cases have occurred recently. It is possible that the two children were kidnapped from elsewhere, making it difficult to investigate. When questioned, both defendants spoke in their local dialect, with Chinese Police Chief Shi En acting as interpreter. They insisted that they had no children and spent money to buy adopted children, not to sell them. Their answers were evasive, and they asked for leniency from the court. Judge Wu ordered them to be remanded in custody separately and scheduled a sentencing date.

Li Suqin Violently Assaulted 146

Li Suqin, a 17-year-old female performer from Nanjing, lives at No. 6, Sanyili, Rue Cardinal Foch, in the French Concession. She has been performing as a Hua Dan actress at the Minle Theater on Rue du Pere Froc for a monthly salary of 100 yuan and is quite popular with the audience. Her elderly father, Li Junqing, and her cousin, Li Zhongxiang, accompany her every day. However, yesterday (17th) at around 8:00 PM, after dinner, Suqin was accompanied by her father and cousin to the theater as usual. When they reached the intersection of Caishi Road, two unidentified men harassed them. Then, emboldened by lust, one of them stopped Suqin, embraced her, and forcibly tried to kiss her. Li's father and cousin were shocked and tried to stop them. The men became enraged and struck Li Zhong twice. They then ordered nearby thugs to take out iron rods and beat Li Zhong, causing him to be injured and fall to the ground. Patrolmen arrived and arrested one of the men, while the others fled. The arrested man was taken to the police station. After questioning, he gave his name as Zhang Fuchun, 45, from Tianjin, and admitted to the assault. He was ordered to be detained. Meanwhile, the injured man was sent to the hospital for treatment. Yesterday, Zhang was sent to the Second Special District Court. Affair Discovered 147

Husband Commits Suicide in Anger 148

Yang Asi, 28 years old, from Yancheng, worked as a rickshaw puller. His wife, Bai, worked as a factory worker in a cotton mill. They lived together at No. 387 Qiwupu Road, Yangshupu. The couple lived a simple life and were considered to be harmonious. They had a child together. Recently, Yang learned that his wife was having an affair. He tried to persuade her to stop, but she refused to admit it, leading to arguments. Yesterday, while she was at work, Yang became resentful and despondent. He felt that life was meaningless and wanted to end his life. He went out and bought opium, which he secretly took. At around 9:00 PM, Bai returned home from work and found her husband lying on the bed, moaning. She asked him what was wrong, but he did not answer. She sent him to Hudong Hospital, but treatment was ineffective, and he soon died. The hospital reported to the Yulin Road Police Station, who sent detectives to investigate. The corpse was taken to the forensic examination office on Avenue Petain. Yesterday morning, a report was submitted to the First Special District Court, and Prosecutor Guo Wei, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan, court clerk, and others, went to the office to examine the body. According to Yang Bai, 23 years old, she had claimed that when she returned home last night, she saw him lying on the bed, appearing ill. She did not know that he had taken poison, so she sent him to the hospital. She said that his sudden suicide was likely due to a lack of money, as he had incurred a lot of debt when he was ill last year. She denied having any improper affairs. Guo accepted her statement and ordered that the examination confirm that the deceased, Yang Asi, had died from opium poisoning. The corpse was released to his wife, Yang Bai, with a written guarantee for coffin preparation.

The International Trade Bureau Compiles the 21st Year Trade Report: The International Trade Bureau originally compiled quarterly trade reports every year. The trade reports for the third and fourth quarters of the previous year have now been compiled, including the annual trade report for the 21st year. It is divided into seven sections: (1) International Economic Situation, (2) Domestic Economic Situation, (3) Import and Export Trade Value Situation, (4) Import and Export Trade Commodity Situation, (5) Import and Export Trade Country Situation, (6) Import and Export Trade Port Situation, (7) Conclusion, including 61 statistical tables and 8 statistical charts. Reader Advisory 164

The Reading Problem of Impoverished Youth 165

Inquiry from Mr. Long Weiyang, Yichang

Having received your reply, I am deeply grateful for your guidance. However, you stated that the current schools are established for the wealthy, and what they teach is also in support of the wealthy. Since you have no money, there is no need to attend these schools. Yes, it is true that without money, how can one attend school? However, in today's China, the number of people without money probably accounts for eight or nine out of ten of the country's population. If one cannot attend school without money, then will the general impoverished youth not all end up without the opportunity to read? What I want to ask you now is: Can we break the boundaries of money and find an opportunity for those without money to have access to books? As for striving and working hard, of course, there is no such thing as not succeeding. However, without the means to become wealthy, no matter how hard you strive or how much you work, you will not find a way, and it will be of no help. Oh, esteemed Mr. Mentor of the People, please give me some guidance!

Answer: Under the current social system and political situation in China, impoverished youth naturally do not have the opportunity to formally enter schools to study. However, this does not mean that our youth cannot read or have the opportunity to read. In Yichang, we do not know the situation; we are in Shanghai, so let us take Shanghai as an example. In Shanghai, there are now many places where ordinary young shop assistants and out-of-school youth can have the opportunity to read. Because public libraries are gradually being established, for example, our circulating library has an average of 300 people reading books every day. In addition, libraries in chambers of commerce and other places are probably the same. Extending from this, the number of people will increase in the future. In this way, are we not invisibly creating many self-study opportunities in society? Moreover, we have specially set up a Reader Advisory column for readers to ask questions, which we feel is creating an opportunity for impoverished youth to have access to books, and the effect will be even greater than formal schools. This is what we dare to predict. If all provinces and regions follow suit, it is not impossible. You can work hard in Yichang to promote these undertakings. As the saying goes, "If you want to establish yourself, establish others; if you want to succeed, help others succeed."

Educational News 166

Important News 167

Ministry of Education Issues Order 168

Measures to Promote the National Language 169

(Nanjing, 20th) The Ministry of Education, based on the resolution submitted by the National National Language Promotion Association, has supplemented the four measures to promote the national language and urged all departments to notify all bookstores within their jurisdiction that, starting from August 1st, all printed elementary school textbooks, children's reading materials, and various books and magazines must be handled in accordance with the following: Publications that do not meet the standard national pronunciation should be stopped from being printed. The publications that do not meet the standard national pronunciation are: 1. Add phonetic symbols to the new characters in elementary school textbooks and the easily misread characters in reading materials. 2. Children's and public reading materials must be compiled in the national language and accompanied by phonetic symbols. 3. At a minimum, phonetic symbols must be added to the titles of various books, magazines, and other printed materials.

10,000 Yuan in Subsidies to Zhejiang University 171

Yesterday, Guo Renyuan, the new president of Zhejiang University, sent personnel to collect the funds. The Department of Finance allocated 10,000 yuan, which the staff member took back for use.

Ministry of Education Promulgates 173

Regulations for Primary and Secondary School Teacher Training (2) 174

Chapter 5 Curriculum 175

Article 26 The teaching subjects and weekly teaching hours of primary schools are listed in the table below.

Article 27 Primary school subjects may be appropriately combined or divided according to local conditions. The methods are as follows:

(1) The three subjects of society, nature, and hygiene may be combined into a common sense subject in elementary schools.

(2) Agricultural and industrial arts and crafts in the labor course may be set up as a single type, that is, the set type is named as a certain course, and the remaining necessary operations are incorporated into the various subjects with similar properties.

(3) The art course in the lower grades may be combined with the labor course and called the work course.

Article 28 The primary school curriculum should be in accordance with the curriculum standards stipulated by the Ministry of Education.

Article 29 Primary school textbooks shall be selected and adopted by the school in accordance with the provisions of Article 9 of the Primary School Law.

Article 30 Primary school teaching should strive to adapt to the physical and mental development of children to stimulate their automatic ability and cultivate national spirit. Subjects such as national language and society should guide them to use and supplement reading materials. Subjects such as nature and labor should focus on experiments and practical work.

Article 31 Local teaching materials in each region shall be compiled by the competent educational administrative organs and submitted to the higher-level educational administrative organs for submission to the Ministry of Education for approval.

Article 32 The content of the primary school curriculum, except for those who have textbooks edited or approved by the Ministry of Education for reference, shall be formulated separately by the educational administrative organs in charge of each province and city in accordance with the provisions of the curriculum standards.

Chapter 6 Moral Education 176

Article 33 Primary school moral education should focus on civic training. Teachers should use various legal activities inside and outside the classroom and actively guide them in conjunction with families and local public institutions.

Article 34 Primary schools, in order to train children's group life, should carry out various group activities and guide children to organize autonomous groups.

Article 35 Primary schools may implement a counselor system for the convenience of individual moral education. All primary school teachers are responsible for directly educating children.

Article 36 Primary schools should contact children's parents at any time to discuss practical issues related to teaching and training in order to improve the efficiency of teaching and training.

Article 37 Corporal punishment shall not be inflicted on primary school children.

Article 38 Primary school children should wear uniforms except in special circumstances. Their clothing supplies should be limited to domestic products.

Article 39 The standards and implementation methods for primary school civic training shall be in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Education.

Article 40 The moral education matters for each semester and each week of primary schools shall be formulated by various localities in accordance with the primary school civic training standards and in consideration of local needs.

Chapter 7 Facilities 177

Article 41 The site of the primary school should be chosen at a location convenient for children to attend school and must have a good environment.

Article 42 Primary school buildings should be simple, sturdy, suitable for teaching management and hygiene, and should use domestic models and materials.

Article 43 Primary schools should have sports fields, workshops, farms or campuses, and the area should be sufficient for application.

Article 44 The desks and chairs used by primary school children should be suitable for the proportion of children's height.

Article 45 Primary schools should refer to the school health facilities plan and strive to enrich the equipment related to hygiene and sports.

Article 46 Primary schools should strive to enrich equipment such as national books, instruments, and appliances.

Article 47 Primary schools should have various important books, registers, charts, etc. about teaching and moral education.

Article 48 The standards for primary school equipment shall be determined separately by the Ministry of Education.

Chapter 8 Achievement Examination 178

Article 49 Primary school children's academic achievement examination, in addition to regular examinations, shall also hold temporary trials, semester examinations, and graduation examinations.

Article 50 Temporary trials shall be held by educators at the end of each month. At least three times must be held in each semester.

Article 51 Semester examinations shall be held by teachers at the end of the semester. However, the semester examination shall be exempted for the semester before graduation, and the usual grades shall be used as the semester grades.

Article 52 The graduation examination shall be held by the primary school principal in conjunction with the teachers of each subject before graduation.

Article 53 The method for calculating the grades of each subject for primary school children, the methods for examining conduct and physical education, and the methods for promoting and downgrading children shall be formulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and record.

Chapter 9 School Year, Years, and Holidays 179

Date 180

Article 54 The primary school shall begin the school year on August 1st of each year and end on July 31st of the following year.

Article 55 One school year is divided into two semesters, with August 1st to January 31st of the following year as the first semester, and February 1st to July 31st as the second semester.

Article 56 The dates of primary school holidays shall be determined separately by the Ministry of Education. Except for the specified dates, holidays or class suspensions shall not be arbitrarily taken.

Article 57 Primary schools located in rural areas may, if there are special circumstances, appropriately move the summer vacation dates according to the agricultural conditions of the school location, and the vacation period may be divided into several sections for interval vacations (such as separate wheat holidays, autumn harvest holidays, etc., while reducing the summer vacation dates, but the total number of vacation dates shall not exceed the prescribed number of summer vacation days and must be approved by the educational administrative organs in charge of the provinces and cities.

Article 58 The beginning and end of the winter and summer vacation dates may be appropriately changed in the provinces and cities with severe cold and hot weather according to local conditions, but the total number of vacation dates shall not exceed the regulations for school vacation dates.

Chapter 10 Enrollment and Graduation 181

Article 59 The enrollment age for primary school children is six full years old, but in special circumstances, it may be postponed to nine full years old.

Article 60 Primary schools should accept transfer students at any time within three months after the start of each semester when there are vacancies in each grade.

Article 61 Primary school children may suspend school for one semester or one academic year due to special physical or family circumstances and return to school after the expiration of the term.

Article 62 Primary school children may be allowed to transfer or withdraw from school if the school verifies that there are special circumstances in their physical or family conditions.

Article 63 Primary school children who have completed their studies and passed the examination shall be given a graduation certificate by the school in accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of the Primary School Law.

Article 64 The graduation of senior primary school children shall be approved by the educational administrative organs in charge and submitted to the higher-level educational administrative organs for approval to hold a graduation joint examination. The methods shall be in accordance with the regulations on the joint examination for graduation of primary and secondary schools promulgated by the Ministry of Education.

Chapter 11 Tuition and Other Expenses 182

Article 65 Primary schools do not charge tuition fees, but except for compulsory education experimental areas, they may, according to local conditions, apply to the educational administrative organs in charge for approval in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the Primary School Law and collect them appropriately.

Article 66 Primary schools that charge tuition fees should still set up free places for more than one-third of impoverished children.

Article 67 Primary schools shall not discriminate against children who are exempt from fees, and the collection of fees shall not be used as a standard for establishing grades.

Article 68 Primary schools shall not collect miscellaneous fees from children.

Article 69 The necessary school supplies, etc., for primary schools may be issued by the school or sold to children at extremely low prices by the school or the local education administrative organs organizing consumer cooperatives.

Article 70 Primary schools shall not collect any fees from children except for special circumstances that have been specially approved by the educational administrative organs in charge and may solicit temporary donations for construction from more wealthy children's families.

Chapter 12 Teachers and Staff 183

Article 71 Primary schools shall have one principal, one teacher for each grade, and may add specialist teachers or assistant teachers as appropriate, but the average number of teachers per two grades shall be limited to three at most.

Article 72 Primary schools should exclusively or jointly set up school doctors or nurses, and those with six grades or more may set up clerks as appropriate, but they must apply to the educational administrative organs in charge for approval.

Article 73 Primary school teachers and staff should live in the school or the area where the school is located.

Article 74 The primary school principal is in charge of all school affairs, in addition to teaching subjects, and guides teachers and staff to share school affairs and training matters.

Article 75 Graduates of normal universities and education departments of university education colleges, graduates of higher normal schools or specialist normal schools, graduates of undergraduate courses of old-style normal schools or senior high school normal departments or special normal departments may be grade teachers or specialist teachers.

Article 76 Primary school grade and specialist teachers who do not have one of the qualifications listed in the preceding article shall be subject to the examination of the primary school teacher examination committee organized by the educational administrative organs in charge.

Article 77 The examination of primary school grade and specialist teachers is divided into two types: non-examination examination and examination examination. Non-examination examination is decided by examining their various certificates (graduation certificate, completion certificate, service certificate, works, etc.). Examination examination, in addition to examining their various certificates, is also examined.

Article 78 Those who have one of the following qualifications may be subject to non-examination examination:

(1) Graduated from schools above the old-style middle school or senior high school, has been a primary school teacher for more than a year, or has attended summer schools run by local education administrative organs or university education colleges and normal schools to make up for education courses for two summer periods.

(2) Graduated from a two-year or more normal training course, or a simplified normal school simplified normal department, has been a primary school teacher for two years or more, or has made up for it in the above-mentioned summer school for three summer periods.

(3) Has been a primary school teacher for more than three years, and the education administrative organs believe that there are indeed achievements, or has made up for it in the above-mentioned summer school for four summer periods.

(4) Has been a primary school teacher for more than three years, and has published special works on primary school education, which the education administrative organs in charge believe are indeed valuable.

Article 79 Those who have one of the following qualifications may be subject to examination examination:

(1) Has graduated from an old-style middle school or senior high school.

(2) Has graduated from a normal school or senior high school for one year and has been a primary school teacher for more than one year.

(3) Has graduated from a normal training course, a simplified normal school or a simplified normal department.

(4) Has been a primary school teacher for more than three years.

(5) Has expertise and has been a primary school teacher for more than one year.

Article 80 The Regulations on the Examination of Primary School Teachers and the Regulations on the Organization of the Committee for the Examination of Primary School Teachers shall be determined separately by the Ministry of Education.

Article 81 Teachers who have one of the qualifications in Article 75 or who have passed the examination and have been in service for more than two years and have achieved results may be primary school principals.

Article 82 Primary school teachers shall be hired by the principal in accordance with the provisions of Article 12 of the Primary School Law one month before the start of the school year. After the hiring is finalized, it shall be reported to the educational administrative organs in charge for record. If there are any unqualified persons, the educational administrative organs in charge may order the original school to rehire.

Article 83 When a primary school is unable to hire teachers with the qualifications stipulated in Article 75 or who have been examined due to special local circumstances, it may use those with one of the qualifications stipulated in Article 79 as substitute teachers, but it shall apply to the educational administrative organs in charge for approval.

Article 84 The salary grade of primary school teachers and staff should be differentiated according to their academic qualifications and experience, but at least it should be twice the personal living expenses in the school location as the standard.

Article 85 The salaries of primary school teachers and staff who are calculated on a monthly basis shall be calculated for twelve months each year.

Article 86 Primary school teachers and staff shall be on campus for at least seven hours per day, and the teaching time shall be at most 300 minutes per day.

Article 87 Female primary school teachers and staff should be given six weeks of rest during the production period, and the salary of their agent should be paid separately by the school to the educational administrative organs in charge.

Article 88 Primary school teachers who continue to work in a school for 12 years may take a year off to engage in research and study and send their results to the original school for submission to the educational administrative organs in charge. The above-mentioned vacation teachers shall still be paid their original salaries, but shall not hold any paid positions concurrently.

Article 89 The salary grade table and annual merit increase methods for primary school teachers and staff shall be stipulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs and submitted to the Ministry of Education for record and implementation.

Article 90 The pension and pension methods for primary school teachers and staff shall be handled in accordance with the Regulations on Pension and Pension for School Teachers and Staff promulgated by the National Government.

Article 91 Primary school teachers and staff shall not be dismissed unless one of the following circumstances exists:

(1) Violation of the criminal law with conclusive evidence; (2) Improper behavior or bad habits; (3) Arbitrary absenteeism; (4) Poor performance; (5) Physical disability or chronic illness that prevents them from performing their duties.

Article 92 The Regulations on the Appointment, Treatment and Guarantee of Primary School Teachers shall be determined separately by the Ministry of Education.

Article 93 Primary school teachers who have made outstanding achievements in further studies shall be rewarded with salary increases or promotions, and the methods for further studies and rewards shall be formulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation.

Actively Engaged in Jiangxi Education Circles 184

National Salvation and Bandit Suppression Efforts

Purchasing Goods to Send to the Frontline Bandit Suppression Soldiers

Purchasing the Jiangxi Education Aircraft

(Nanchang Correspondence) The educational circles of Jiangxi province, recognizing the importance of bandit suppression work, and in order to concentrate the power of the education sector and assist in bandit suppression, have organized the Provincial Education Circles Assistance to Bandit Suppression Committee. The committee has decided on methods for the education sector to assist in bandit suppression, dividing them into two types: material assistance and spiritual assistance. In terms of material assistance, it was resolved to donate funds for bandit suppression during the bandit suppression period, including: (1) Teachers and staff of provincial secondary schools and above and educational institutions will donate 20% of their salaries uniformly. (2) Teachers and staff of primary schools in the provincial capital and teachers and staff of public and private secondary schools in cities and counties will donate 10% of their salaries uniformly. (3) Teachers and staff of public and private primary schools in cities and counties will donate 5% of their salaries uniformly. (4) Students of all levels of schools will donate freely. This donation from provincial schools and educational institutions amounts to nearly 20,000 yuan per month. In addition, each school will produce straw sandals, bamboo hats, etc., or purchase and collect towels, soap, socks, pastries, and other military supplies to donate to the bandit suppression army. Spiritual assistance includes propaganda and consolation work. In addition to organizing parades in the provincial capital to publicize the cruelty of the Red bandits and the importance of assisting in bandit suppression, each school has also established a method of collecting consolation bags. The bags are six inches long and four inches wide, filled with candies, snacks, towels, socks, cigarettes, etc., along with consolation letters or messages. Each student is required to prepare one bag, with a cost limit of one dime. Within a few days, more than 14,000 bags have been collected and sent to the front by the Department of Education to be distributed to the bandit suppression soldiers. The Department of Education has also issued a circular to all schools in other districts to follow suit, but instead, they are changed to consolation donations, collecting according to the amount and handing it over to the Department of Education to purchase goods and transfer them as gifts, it is said.

Regarding the aviation national salvation movement, Jiangxi education circles have also decided on a method to undertake the fundraising of 120,000 yuan for aviation national salvation donations to purchase an aircraft, named the Jiangxi Education. The methods for allocating and controlling the fundraising are as follows: (1) There are approximately 100,000 primary school students in the province, each donating at least 4 dimes, totaling 40,000 yuan. (2) There are approximately 10,000 secondary school students and above in the province, each donating at least 2 yuan, totaling 20,000 yuan. (3) There are approximately 600 students receiving subsidies from national universities outside the province and publicly funded students studying abroad, each donating at least 10 yuan, totaling 6,000 yuan. (4) Teachers and staff of each school and staff of social education institutions should donate 5% of their salary for a period of six months, with approximately 30,000 yuan from provincial education institutions and approximately 15,000 yuan from county public and private education institutions. (5) The Provincial Education Department will organize the Provincial Education Circles Aviation National Salvation Committee to collect the above donations after the assistance to bandit suppression donations are stopped. If the amount is insufficient, the committee will be responsible for fundraising. This method has now been implemented by the Education Department.

Meeting of the Board of Directors of the Chinese Social Education Society 186

Annual Meeting to be Held in Jinan Starting August 20th

Rural Construction and National Rejuvenation as the Focus of Discussion

The Chinese Social Education Society held its fourth board of directors meeting on the 18th at the Nanjing People's Education Hall of Jiangsu Province. Those present included Niu Yongjian, Chen Lijiang, Gan Yuyuan, Dong Huai, Zhao Mian, Shang Zhongyi, Peng Baichuan, Sun Fang, Li Zheng, Gao Yang, and those attending as observers, Zhu Jianbai, Zhao Guangtao, etc., more than ten people. Niu Yongjian chaired in the morning, and Chen Lijiang chaired in the afternoon. Many cases were resolved. The main points are recorded as follows: (1) Approved 122 new individual members, including Cao Chu, etc., and 60 social education institutions, including the Fujian Provincial Library, etc., as group members. (2) The executive director and general director, Yu Qingtang, requested leave to go to Denmark to investigate popular education; Chen Lijiang was publicly recommended to act in his place. (3) It was determined that the second annual meeting of this year would be held in Jinan, Shandong from August 20th to 24th, and members Kong Jing'an and Dong Weichuan were appointed to be responsible for preparations. (4) It was resolved that rural construction and national rejuvenation would be the center of discussion for the second annual meeting, and Liang Shuming, Gao Jianfu, Chen Lijiang, Zhuang Zexuan, Meng Xiancheng, etc., were appointed to form groups to draft plans to be submitted to the next board meeting for discussion. (5) Liang Shuming, Niu Yongjian, Gao Jianfu, and Meng Xiancheng were re-elected, along with Chen Lijiang, Shu Xincheng, and Yu Qingtang, who were appointed at the previous meeting, as members of the Social Education System Reorganization Committee, and Chen Lijiang was designated to convene it. (6) Peng Baichuan, Zhao Guangtao, Zhu Jianbai, Dong Weichuan, Lei Binnan, Sun Zhongwei, and Ma Zongrong were appointed to be responsible for coordinating domestic art and health institutions, groups, and social education institutions to fully mobilize to implement anti-Japanese national salvation education. (7) It was resolved that, in addition to adding a method for the Society to organize a Northwest Education Inspection Group, the original plan for developing social education in the Central Plains and Northwest would be adopted. (8) It was resolved to send a circular to social education institutions in various places to encourage popular self-defense training. (9) Zhao Guangtao, Gao Jianfu, and Chen Dabai were appointed to draft a plan for establishing a popular education experimental zone, with the location set near Luoyang, in order to cooperate with the Central Plains Social Education Center in its management. (10) It was resolved to compile and print two types of social education series within this year. (11) Passed the Society's method for introducing social education service personnel and the Society's method for registering contracted members.
